6 min
The Principle of Not Returning Spoils to the Enemy
Short usul principle on spoils in dar al-harb

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle prohibiting the return of spoils to the enemy in dar al-harb when danger persists, and apply it to a scenario.

Core Idea
Returning spoils to a dangerous enemy strengthens them; Hanafi law forbids it.

War is a serious matter, and the spoils of war are not mere property. The Hanafi tradition derives a clear principle from the Quran and Sunnah: when there is a risk that the enemy might regain strength and attack again, returning captured spoils is prohibited. This lesson unpacks that principle and its rationale.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Context
Recognize that 'dar al-harb' denotes enemy territory during active hostilities. The 'spoils' include captives, weapons, and goods. The principle applies only when there is a tangible danger of the enemy regrouping.
The condition of 'danger' is key; if absent, the ruling may differ.
2
Memorize the Principle
Learn the exact wording: 'In dar al-harb, if there is danger, do not hand over the spoils to them, so that they do not have the courage to attack again.' Both the Arabic and English formulations are essential for recall.
The rationale is explicitly stated: preventing enemy morale and capability.
3
Identify the Legal Ruling
The principle generates a prohibition (haram) or at least makruh tahrimi. The act of handing over spoils when danger exists is an unlawful act. Note that this is not a mere recommendation but a binding rule.
This ruling is derived from the Quranic commands to keep captives until the war ends (Surah Muhammad, 47:4) and to fight polytheists (Surah al-Tawba, 9:5).
4
Apply to a New Scenario
Take a situation: Muslim forces capture enemy supplies and prisoners. The enemy has fled but is known to be reorganizing in a nearby valley. According to the principle, return is prohibited. Consider how the condition of 'danger' is assessed.
The principle serves as a guide for commanders and judges in wartime.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اصول: دار حرب میں خطرہ ہو تو مال غنیمت کو ان کے حوالہ نہ کرے، تاکہ دوبارہ حملہ کرنے کی ہمت نہ ہو۔
Principle: In dar al-harb, if there is danger, do not hand over the spoils to them, so that they do not have the courage to attack again.
Source pages p. 372

Commentary
This is a brief usul (principle) that summarizes the rationale behind the earlier rulings: spoils (including captives and goods) captured from the enemy in dar al-harb must not be returned to them, especially when there is a risk of them regrouping and attacking again. Returning spoils would strengthen the enemy's morale and resources. The principle is derived from the Quranic command to kill and capture polytheists (Surah al-Tawba 9:5) and to keep captives until the war ends (Surah Muhammad 47:4). This principle underlies the Hanafi prohibition against returning captives or distributing spoils on the battlefield.

Key Terms
اصول (usul): A legal maxim or principle derived from the sources, guiding rulings in similar cases.
دار حرب (dar al-harb): Enemy territory where hostilities are ongoing.
مال غنیمت (mal ghanimat): Spoils of war, including movables, captives, and other property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the purpose of not handing over spoils to the enemy in dar al-harb according to this principle?
A) To increase Muslim wealth
B) To prevent the enemy from regaining strength to attack
C) To fulfill a treaty
D) To discourage future wars

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school strictly prohibits returning spoils to the enemy in dar al-harb when danger persists, as it would embolden them to attack again.

Reinforcements Share in Spoils Before Securing
Ruling on reinforcements sharing spoils if they join before ikhraz.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on reinforcements joining before spoils are secured and apply the two Companion proofs to similar scenarios.

Core Idea
Reinforcements share equally if they arrive while spoils are still in dar al-harb.

This lesson extends the previous rule on division of spoils. The matn of al-Quduri addresses a common scenario: reinforcements (madad) arrive after the battle is won but before the spoils are moved to dar al-Islam. The Hanafi school holds that they share equally, supported by the practice of Abu Bakr and Umar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling scenario
The passage specifies: reinforcements join the main army in dar al-harb before the spoils have been secured (ukhrizat) in dar al-Islam.
2
Extract the hukm
The matn states they 'share with them in it' (sharakuhum fiha), which is wajib according to the Hanafi school.
3
Analyze the first proof (Abu Bakr)
Ziyad ibn Labid included reinforcements under Ikrimah after the conquest of al-Najir, despite the battle being over, because spoils were still in dar al-harb.
This shows that ikhraz (securing in dar al-Islam) is the criterion, not participation in battle.
4
Analyze the second proof (Umar)
Umar instructed Sa'd at al-Qadisiyyah to give shares to reinforcements who arrived before the army dispersed (yatafaqqalu).
This reinforces the principle that timing before dispersal/ikhraz is key.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِنْ لَحَقَهُمْ مَدَدٌ فِي دَارِ الْحَرْبِ قَبْلَ أَنْ يُخْرِزُوا الْغَنِيمَةَ بِدَارِ الْإِسْلَامِ شَارَكُوهُمْ فِيهَا
اس وجه (۱) قول الصحابي لثبوت فَإِنْ لَحِقَهُمْ مَدَدٌ فِي دَارِ الحَرْبِ \ أَنَّ أَبَا بَكْرِ الصَّدِّيقَ فيه بَعَثَ عِكْرِمَةَ بْنَ أبي جَهْل فِي خَمْسِمِائَةٍ مِنَ الْمُسْلِمِينَ مَدَدًا لِزِيَادِ بْن لَبِيدٍ وَلِلْمُهَاجِر بن أَبي أُمَيَّةَ، فَوَافَقَهُمُ الْجُنْدُ قَدِ افْتَتَحُوا النَّجِيرَ بِالْيَمِينِ، فَأَشْرَكَهُمْ زِيَادُ بْنُ لَبِيدٍ وَهُوَ مِمَّنْ شَهِدَ بَدْرًا فِي الْغَنِيمَةِ (السنن الكبري للبيهقي، بَابُ الْغَنِيمَةِ لِمَنْ شَهِدَ الْوَقْعَةَ ، [غبر؟] 17952)
وجه : (۲) قول الصحابي لثبوت فَإِنْ لَحَقَهُمْ مَدَدٌ فِي دَارِ الْحَرْبِ قَالَ: كَتَبَ عُمَرُ إِلَى سَعْدٍ يَوْمَ الْقَادِسِيَّةِ: «إِنِّي قَدْ بَعَثْتُ إِلَيْكَ أَهْلَ الْحِجَازِ وَأَهْلَ الشَّامِ، فَمَنْ أَدْرَكَ مِنْهُمُ الْقِتَالَ قَبْلَ أَنْ يَتَفَقَّلُوا فَأَسْهِمْ لَهُمْ» (مصنف ابن شيبه فِي الْقَوْمِ يَجِينُونَ بَعْدَ الْوَقْعَةِ هَلْ لَهُمْ شَيْءٌ، [غبر؟] 33222)
And if reinforcements join them in dar al-harb before they secure the spoils in dar al-Islam, they share with them in it. This is proof 1: Saying of the Companion for establishing 'then if reinforcements join them in dar al-harb': That Abu Bakr al-Siddiq sent Ikrimah ibn Abi Jahl with five hundred Muslims as reinforcements for Ziyad ibn Labid and al-Muhajir ibn Abi Umayyah, and they met the army that had conquered al-Najir in Yemen, so Ziyad ibn Labid (who was a Badri) included them in the spoils. Proof 2: Saying of the Companion for establishing 'then if reinforcements join them in dar al-harb': He said: Umar wrote to Sa'd on the day of al-Qadisiyyah: 'I have sent to you the people of Hijaz and the people of Sham, so whoever among them reaches the fighting before they return (depart), give them a share.'
Source pages p. 373

Commentary
This ruling extends the previous principle: reinforcements (madad) that catch up with the main army while still in dar al-harb, before the spoils have been moved to dar al-Islam, are entitled to a share. The text provides two proofs from the actions of the Companions (qawl al-sahabi). First, Abu Bakr sent reinforcements under Ikrimah to Ziyad ibn Labid, and when they arrived after the conquest of al-Najir, Ziyad included them in the spoils despite having already conquered the area. Second, Umar instructed Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas at al-Qadisiyyah to give shares to reinforcements who arrived before the army dispersed from the battlefield. These show that the key factor is whether the spoils have been 'secured' (ikhraz) in dar al-Islam; as long as they are still in dar al-harb, even after victory, new arrivals share equally.

Key Terms
مَدَد (madad): Reinforcements sent to support an army already in the field.
أَخْرَز / يُخْرِز (akhraza / yukhrizu): To secure or bring to a safe place; here, bringing spoils to dar al-Islam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What did Abu Bakr do when reinforcements under Ikrimah arrived after the conquest of al-Najir?
A) Gave them no share because they missed the battle.
B) Included them in the spoils because the spoils were still in dar al-harb.
C) Gave them a smaller share than the original fighters.
D) Sent them back without any spoils.

Key Takeaway
Reinforcements joining before spoils are secured in dar al-Islam share equally; the condition is ikhraz, not participation in battle.

Market People Have No Right to Spoils Unless They Fight
Ruling with two proofs establishing non-entitlement of non-combatant traders to war spoils.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the entitlement of market people (ahl suq al-askar) to war spoils and apply the proofs (Qawl Sahabi and hadith) to determine when they receive a share.

Core Idea
Non-combatant traders get no share of spoils until they personally fight.

When an army marches, merchants often accompany it to sell goods. The Hanafi school addresses their status regarding war spoils (ghanimah). Does mere presence in the camp entitle them to a share? The text rules that they have no right unless they actively participate in combat. Two proofs are cited: a letter from Umar ibn al-Khattab and a hadith from Salamah ibn al-Akwa'. This lesson unpacks the ruling and its evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject of the ruling
Determine who 'ahl suq al-askar' are: traders and merchants who accompany the army but do not fight. They are not soldiers.
Compare with soldiers, volunteers, and support personnel.
2
State the default ruling
The text clearly says 'no right' (la haqq) for them in the spoils. This is the default Hanafi position.
The exception is introduced with 'illa' — unless they fight.
3
Examine the first proof: Qawl Sahabi of Umar
Umar wrote: 'Indeed the spoils are for those who witnessed the battle.' The word 'shahid al-waq'ah' implies active presence in fighting, not mere physical presence in the camp.
This is a strong precedent from a Companion and caliph.
4
Examine the second proof: Hadith of Salamah ibn al-Akwa'
Salamah served Talhah at al-Hudaybiyyah, watering his horse. Later, the Prophet gave Salamah shares of a horseman and foot soldier. However, this does not set a precedent for all non-combatants; Salamah was a servant in a support role and likely also fought in other engagements.
The Hanafi interpretation limits this to those who directly support combatants in battle, not general traders.
5
Understand the cross-madhhab difference
Some schools (e.g., Shafi'i, Hanbali) extend a share to those who provide support like watering horses, based on broader utility. The Hanafi school restricts it to actual fighters.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf with practical consequences.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا حَقَّ لِأَهْلِ سُوقِ الْعَسْكَر فِي الْغَنِيمَةِ إِلَّا أَنْ يُقَاتِلُوا
وجه : (۱) قول الصحابى لثبوت وَلَا حَقَّ لِأَهْلِ سُوقِ الْعَسْكَر في الْغَنِيمَة \ قَالَ: كَتَبَ عُمَرُ بنُ الْخَطَّابِ: إِنَّ الْغَنِيمَةَ لِمَنْ شَهِدَ الْوَقْعَةَ (السنن الكبري للبيهقي، الْغَنِيمَة لِمَنْ شَهِدَ الْوَقْعَةَ، [غبر؟] 17954)
وجه:(۲) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا حَقَّ لِأَهْلِ سُوقِ الْعَسْكَرِ فِي الْغَنِيمَةِ حَدَّثَنِي إِيَاسُ بْنُ سَلَمَةَ. حَدَّثَنِي أَبي قَالَ: قَدِمْنَا الْحَدَيْبِيَةَ مَعَ رَسُولِ اللهِ .. ونحن أَرْبَعَ عَشْرَةَ مِائَةٌ. وَعَلَيْهَا خَمْسُونَ شَاةً لَا تُزويها ..... وَكُنْتُ تَبِيعًا لِطَلْحَةَ بْن عُبَيْدِ اللَّهِ . أَسْقِي فَرَسَهُ، وَأَحُسُهُ، وَأَخْدِمُهُ. وَآكُلُ مِنْ طَعَامِهِ. .... قَالَ: ثُمَّ أَعْطَانِي رَسُولُ اللَّهِ سَهْمَ الْفَارِسِ وَسَهْمَ الرَّاجِلِ (مسلم شريف، بَاب غَزْوَةِ ذِي قَرَدٍ وَغَيْرهَا ، [غبر؟] 1807)
اصول مال غنیمت میں مجاہدین کا حق ثابت ہو جائے تو مد والوں کو اس میں حصہ نہیں ملے گا۔
And there is no right for the people of the army market in the spoils unless they fight. Proof 1: Saying of the Companion for establishing 'and no right for the people of the army market in the spoils': He said: Umar ibn al-Khattab wrote: 'Indeed the spoils are for those who witnessed the battle.' Proof 2: The hadith for establishing 'and no right for the people of the army market in the spoils': Iyas ibn Salamah narrated from his father who said: We arrived at al-Hudaybiyyah with the Messenger of Allah... we were 1400, and we had fifty sheep that did not satisfy... I was a servant of Talhah ibn Ubaydillah; I watered his horse, groomed it, and served him, and ate from his food... Then the Messenger of Allah gave me the share of a horseman and the share of a foot soldier. Principle: When the right of the mujahideen in the spoils is established, the reinforcements do not get a share.
Source pages p. 373

Commentary
This ruling addresses the status of non-combatant individuals present with the army, such as merchants and traders (ahl suq al-askar). The Hanafi position is that they have no automatic right to a share of the spoils unless they actually participate in fighting (yuqatilu). The proofs: (1) Umar's letter stating that spoils are only for those who witnessed the battle, implying that mere presence as a tradesman is insufficient. (2) The hadith of Salamah ibn al-Akwa' (the narrator) who was a servant of Talhah at Hudaybiyyah; despite being a non-combatant, he was given a share of the spoils (presumably from a later expedition) because he functioned in a support role. However, the text seems to use this to illustrate that the default is no share unless one fights or has a clear combat-related role. The Urdu commentary at the end adds that once the mujahideen's right is established, reinforcements (madad) do not get a share unless they fight—this appears to reiterate the general principle. Note: The hadith about Salamah receiving shares may be misinterpreted; the context is that Salamah was a participant in some battles, not just a trader. So the ruling stands: mere traders have no claim.

Key Terms
سُوق الْعَسْكَر (suq al-askar): The market that accompanies an army, consisting of merchants and traders who sell goods to soldiers.
الغَنِيمَة (al-ghanimah): Spoils of war taken from the enemy after a battle.
شَهِدَ الْوَقْعَةَ (shahid al-waq'ah): Witnessed the battle, interpreted by Hanafis as actively participating in combat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under what condition do the people of the army market (ahl suq al-askar) receive a share of the spoils according to the Hanafi school?
A) They always receive a share as camp followers.
B) They receive a share only if they provide medical aid.
C) They receive a share if they actually fight in the battle.
D) They never receive any share under any condition.

Key Takeaway
Market people only get war spoils if they actually engage in combat.

Ruling on Spoils from Non-Muslims Capturing Non-Muslims
States the ruling that spoils taken by non-Muslims from other non-Muslims become lawful for Muslims when they conquer them.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on spoils taken by Muslims from non-Muslims who had captured them from other non-Muslims, and explain the legal reasoning.

Core Idea
Property validly owned by non-Muslims becomes permissible spoils for Muslims upon conquest.

This lesson presents a concise ruling from Al-Quduri's matn on a specific scenario: when non-Muslims fight each other and one group conquers the other, the conquerors own the spoils. Later, if Muslims conquer that group, the spoils they had taken become lawful for the Muslims. This ruling hinges on the transfer of ownership through conquest among non-Muslims, a key principle in Hanafi jurisprudence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rounds of conquest
First, non-Muslims (Turks) conquer other non-Muslims (Romans) and take their property. Second, Muslims conquer the Turks.
2
Determine ownership after the first conquest
The Turks own the property because conquest among non-Muslims transfers ownership in Hanafi law.
Key term: malakuha (they own it)
3
Apply the ruling after Muslim conquest
When Muslims conquer the Turks, the property taken from the Romans becomes lawful spoils for the Muslims.
The matn states: حَلَّ لَنَا (it becomes lawful for us)

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا غَلَبَ التَّرْكُ عَلَى الرُّومِ فَسَبَوْهُمْ وَأَخَذُوا أَمْوَالَهُمْ مَلَكُوهَا . فَإِنْ غَلَبْنَا عَلَى التُّرْكِ حَلَّ لَنَا مَا تَأْخُذُهُ مِنْ ذَلِكَ
And if the Turks overcome the Romans and capture them and take their wealth, they own it. Then if we overcome the Turks, what we take from that [spoils] becomes lawful for us.
Source pages p. 375

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from the matn of Al-Quduri. It addresses a scenario where non-Muslim groups (here, the Turks and Romans) fight among themselves, and one group captures the other and takes their property. According to the Hanafi school, the capturing non-Muslims (the Turks) come to own that property by the fact of conquest (ghalabah). Later, if the Muslims conquer the Turks, the property that the Turks had taken from the Romans becomes lawful spoils for the Muslims. The ruling is based on the principle that the property is no longer owned by the original (Roman) owners, as it was validly owned by the Turks. Thus, upon Muslim conquest, it is treated like any other spoils of war.

Key Terms
غَلَبَ / غَلَبَة (ghalaba / ghalabah): Military conquest and complete control, resulting in ownership of movable property.
مَلَكُوهَا (malakuha): They own it (the property) as a result of conquest.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the matn, if the Turks conquer the Romans and take their property, then Muslims conquer the Turks, what is the ruling on that property for the Muslims?
A) It must be returned to the Romans.
B) It is lawful for the Muslims.
C) It must be destroyed.
D) It remains the property of the Turks.

Key Takeaway
When non-Muslims conquer other non-Muslims and own their property, that property becomes lawful spoils for Muslims upon subsequent conquest.

The Validity of a Slave's Aman: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Presents the Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa invalidates a slave's aman while the Sahibayn validate it, with hadith evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a slave's aman and identify the evidence used by the Sahibayn to support its validity.

Core Idea
A slave's aman is valid because the protection of Muslims is one, supported by explicit prophetic hadith.

This lesson examines a dispute within the Hanafi school: does a Muslim slave have the authority to grant aman (safe conduct) to enemy combatants? While Imam Abu Hanifa held that a slave's aman is invalid due to lack of full authority, his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), considered it valid. The lesson explores their reasoning, the principle of unified Muslim protection (dhimmat al-muslimin wahidah), and the hadith evidence that underpins their view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
State the ruling of Abu Hanifa (invalid) and the Sahibayn (valid) regarding a slave granting aman to enemies.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf, not a cross-madhhab one.
2
Examine the principle of unified protection
Understand the maxim 'dhimmat al-muslimin wahidah' — the protection offered by any Muslim is binding on all Muslims. This is the Sahibayn's foundational reasoning.
This principle also applies to women and minors.
3
Analyze the hadith evidence
Study the hadith from Ali (ra) where the Prophet explicitly says a slave's aman is permissible (ja'iz). Consider its chain (al-Bayhaqi) and its implication for the ruling.
The hadith also mentions that a slave gets only a token from booty, which is a separate ruling.
4
Understand the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
If a slave grants aman, according to Abu Hanifa the enemy is not safe and may still be attacked; according to the Sahibayn, the enemy is safe and must be protected.
The mufta bihi (operative) position is the Sahibayn's view.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Later Hanafi authorities (e.g., al-Hidayah) adopt the Sahibayn's position. Thus, a slave's aman is valid in fatwa.
This shows how later tarjih resolves intra-school differences.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ يَصِحُ أَمَانُهُ وَذِمَّةُ الْمُسْلِمِينَ وَاحِدَةٌ. يَسْعَى بِمَا أَدْنَاهُمْ. مسلم شريف، بَاب فَضْل الْمَدِينَةِ، وَدُعَاءِ النَّبيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم فِيهَا بِالْبَرَكَةِ. وَبَيَانِ تَحْرِيمِهَا وَتَحْرِيم صَيْدِهَا وَشَجَرِهَا وَبَيَانِ حُدُودِ حَرَمِهَ، نمبر 1370) وجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ يَصِحُ أَمَانُهُ عَلِي بْنِ أَبِي طَالِبٍ ، قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم : " لَيْسَ لِلْعَبْدِ مِنَ الْغَنِيمَةِ شَيْءٌ إِلَّا خُرْتَيَ الْمَتَاعِ، وَأَمَانُهُ جَائِزٌ إِذَا هُوَ أَعْطَى الْقَوْمَ الْأَمَانَ "السنن الكبري للبيهقي، بَابُ أَمَانِ الْعَبْدِ، نمبر 18172)
And Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: His (the slave's) aman is valid, and the protection of the Muslims is one, the lowest of them suffices. (Muslim, etc.) And evidence (2) for establishing that Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said his aman is valid: Ali ibn Abi Talib said: The Messenger of Allah said: 'The slave has nothing from the booty except the khurty[؟] of the goods, and his aman is permissible when he gives the people aman.' (al-Bayhaqi)
Source pages p. 375

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of aman (safe conduct) given by a slave to enemy combatants. The text explicitly states the position of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn): the aman of a slave is valid. Their reasoning is that the protection (dhimma) of all Muslims is one, and the lowest among them suffices to grant aman. They support this with a hadith from Ali narrated by al-Bayhaqi, where the Prophet explicitly says that a slave's aman is permissible. Abu Hanifa's view, although not stated here, is that a slave's aman is not valid because the slave does not have independent authority. The Sahibayn's view is considered mufta bihi in later Hanafi practice. The hadith also mentions that a slave has no share in the booty except a small portion of the goods (khurty al-mata'), which is a separate ruling.

Key Terms
أَمَان (aman): Safe conduct granted to enemy combatants, guaranteeing protection of life and property.
ذِمَّةُ الْمُسْلِمِينَ وَاحِدَة (dhimmat al-muslimin wahidah): The protection offered by Muslims is unified and indivisible; the aman of one Muslim is binding on all.
خُرْتَيَ الْمَتَاع (khurty al-mata'): A small portion of the spoils, often interpreted as a token.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, why is the aman of a slave valid?
A) Because the slave is a Muslim and all Muslims' protection is one.
B) Because the slave has the permission of his master.
C) Because the slave can fight in jihad.
D) Because the slave is an adult.

Key Takeaway
The aman of a slave is valid in the Hanafi school, based on the principle of unified Muslim protection and explicit prophetic hadith.

Recovery of Captured Property Before and After Division
Three rulings on property recovery from enemy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three scenarios for recovering property from enemy hands and identify which scenario requires payment or offers an option.

Core Idea
Recovery of captured property depends on timing: before division = free, after division = pay value, trader purchase = option.

When Muslims recapture property that the enemy had previously taken from them, the ruling depends on whether the spoils have been divided. Additionally, if a trader buys such property from enemy territory and brings it to Islamic lands, the original owner retains a special right. This lesson clarifies each scenario so you can apply the correct rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three distinct scenarios
The passage presents three cases: (1) recovery before division of spoils, (2) recovery after division, (3) a trader buying the property from dar al-harb and bringing it to dar al-Islam. Note the condition that triggers each ruling.
2
Determine the obligation in each case
For case 1: original owner takes property for free. For case 2: original owner must pay the value (qimah) to the soldier who received it in division. For case 3: original owner has an option (khiyar) to take it by paying the trader the purchase price or leave it.
The option is not an absolute right; it requires compensation.
3
Understand the legal rationale
Before division, the property is still considered part of the booty that has not been assigned; thus the original owner reclaims it fully. After division, ownership has transferred to the soldier, so compensation is required. For the trader, the purchase is valid but the original owner's right is preserved through the option.
This balances the original owner's right with the new acquirer's good faith.
4
Apply the rulings to a hypothetical
Example: A Muslim's sheep were captured by enemy. Muslims recover them before dividing spoils: the owner takes them free. If recovered after division: owner pays the soldier the sheep's value. If a trader buys them from enemy and brings them to Muslim land: owner may take them by paying the trader the price or leave them with trader.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِنْ ظَهَرَ عَلَيْهَا الْمُسْلِمُونَ فَوَجَدُوهَا قَبْلَ الْقِسْمَةِ فَهِيَ فَهُمْ بِغَيْرِ شَيْءٍ وَإِنْ وَجَدُوهَا بَعْدَ الْقِسْمَةِ أَخَذُوهَا بِالْقِيمَةِ إِنْ أَحَبُّوا وَإِنْ دَخَلَ دَارَ الْحَرْبِ تَاجِرٌ فَاشْتَرَى ذَلِكَ بِثَمَنٍ وَأَخْرَجَهُ إِلَى دَارِ الْإِسْلَامِ فَمَالِكُهُ الْأَوَّلُ بِالْخِيَارِ إِنْ شَاءَ أَخَذَهُ بِالثَّمَنِ الَّذِي اشْتَرَاهُ التَّاجِرُ بِهِ وَإِنْ شَاءَ تَرَكَهُ
Then if the Muslims overcome them (the enemy) and find it (the captured property) before the division, then it is for them without anything (payment). And if they find it after the division, they take it by (paying) the price if they wish. And if a trader enters the abode of war and buys that with a price and brings it out to the abode of Islam, then its first owner has the option: if he wishes he takes it for the price with which the trader bought it, and if he wishes he leaves it.
Source pages p. 376

Commentary
This passage contains two rulings from the matn of Al-Quduri regarding property that was captured by the enemy and then recovered by Muslims. The first ruling: If Muslims recover the property before the division (qismah) of the spoils among the Muslim army, the original owner takes it back without paying anything. This is because the property has not yet been distributed and is considered to have been recovered from enemy hands while still in a state of war. The second ruling: If the property is recovered after the spoils have been divided among the Muslim soldiers, then the original owner may take it back, but he must pay the value (qimah) to the soldier who received it in the division. This is because the soldier has become the owner through the division. The third ruling: If a trader (tajir) goes into dar al-harb (enemy territory) and buys the captured property from the enemy for a price, and then brings it to dar al-Islam, the original owner has the option (khiyar) to either take the property by paying the trader the price he paid, or to leave it with the trader. If he takes it, he pays the price; if he leaves it, the trader remains the owner. This is based on the principle that the original owner's right is not completely lost, but he must compensate the trader who acquired it in good faith.

Key Terms
الْقِسْمَة (al-qismah): The division of spoils among the Muslim army after the battle.
الْخِيَار (al-khiyar): The right of option: the original owner can choose to take back his property by paying the price or leave it.
دَارَ الْحَرْب (dar al-harb): Territory under non-Muslim control where the laws of war apply.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a trader buys captured property from the enemy and brings it to dar al-Islam, what right does the original owner have?
A) He may take it for free.
B) He may take it by paying the trader the price the trader paid.
C) He has no right to reclaim it.
D) He may take it by paying the current market value.

Key Takeaway
The recovery of captured property in Hanafi law depends on timing: before division no payment, after division pay value, and for trader purchase the owner has a compensated option.

Rulings on Tanfil (Extra Reward) During Battle
Ruling with proofs from Quran and Sunnah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which an Imam may grant tanfil during battle and identify when it may only be given from the khums.

Core Idea
The Imam may grant extra spoils during battle to encourage fighters, but after booty is secured, only from the khums.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on al-tanfil (extra reward) during jihad. The text from Al-Quduri's Mukhtasar clarifies that the Imam may promise additional spoils to soldiers while fighting is ongoing, but after the booty is brought securely to Islamic territory, such promises can only be fulfilled from the khums (the fifth portion reserved for the Prophet and public interests). The proofs include a Quranic verse and several hadiths from the Prophet's practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is tanfil — giving extra reward from spoils. The ruling is permissible (la ba's) but conditional.
2
Distinguish the two scenarios
Scenario 1: During battle before booty is secured — general permission from any booty. Scenario 2: After booty is secured in Dar al-Islam — only from the khums.
This is the key condition.
3
Locate the primary proofs
Quran verse (Al-Anfal 8:65) encourages fighting, implying permissibility of incentives. Hadith from Abu Qatada and others show the Prophet giving salab to the killer and promising quarter after khums.
4
Understand the ruling on salab
If the Imam does not specifically assign the salab (belongings of the slain) to the killer, it becomes part of the general booty shared equally.
This complements the tanfil ruling.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Given a hypothetical situation, determine whether tanfil is allowed and from which portion.
Test understanding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ السّير
٢٥ وَلَا بَأْسَ أَنْ يُنْفِلَ الْإِمَامُ فِي حَالِ الْقِتَالِ وَيُحَرِّضَ بِالنَّفْلِ عَلَى الْقَتْلِ فَيَقُولُ مَنْ قَتَلَ قَتِيلًا فَلَهُ سَلَبُهُ ٢٦ و يَقُولُ لِلسَّرِيَّةِ قَدْ جَعَلْت لَكُمْ الرُّبْعَ بَعْدَ الْخُمُسِ ، وَلَا يُنْفِلُ بَعْدَ إِحْرَازِ الْغَنِيمَةِ بِدَارِ الْإِسْلَامِ إِلَّا مِنْ الْخُمْسِ
٢٨ وَإِذَا لَمْ يَجْعَل السَّلَبَ لِلْقَاتِلِ فَهُوَ مِنْ جُمْلَةِ الْغَنِيمَةِ وَالْقَاتِلُ وَغَيْرُهُ فِيهِ سَوَاءٌ

وجه : (۲) الحديث لثبوت وَلا بَأسَ أَنْ يُنْفِلَ الْإِمَامُ فِي حَالِ الْقِتَالِ \ عَنْ أَبِي قَتَادَةَ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «مَنْ قَتَلَ قَتِيلًا لَهُ عَلَيْهِ بَيِّنَةٌ فَلَهُ سَلَبُهُ»» (سنن الترمذى، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي مَنْ قَتَلَ قَتِيلًا فَلَهُ سَلَبُهُ، غبر 1562)
وجه: (١) الحديث لثبوت و يَقُولُ لِلسَّرِيَّةِ قَدْ جَعَلْت لَكُمْ الرُّبْعَ \ عَنْ حَبِيبِ بْنِ مَسْلَمَةَ، «أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم كَانَ يُنَفِّلُ الرُّبْعَ بَعْدَ الْخُمُسِ، وَالقُلُثَ بَعْدَ الْخُمُسِ إِذَا قَفَلَ»(سنن ابوداود، بَابٌ فِيمَنْ قَالَ الْحُمُسُ قَبْلَ النَّفْل، نمبر (2749)
وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يُنْفِلُ بَعْدَ إِحْرَازِ الْغَنِيمَةِ \ سَمِعْتُ عَمْرَو بْنَ عَبَسَةَ، قَالَ: صَلَّى بِنَا رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم إِلَى بَعِيرِ مِنَ المَغْنَم، فَلَمَّا سَلَّمَ أَخَذَ وَبَرَةً مِنْ جَنْبِ الْبَعِيرِ، ثُمَّ قَالَ: «وَلَا يَحِلُّ لِي مِنْ غَنَائِمِكُمْ مِثْلُ هَذَا إِلَّا الْخَمْسُ، وَالخُمُسُ مَرْدُودٌ فِيكُمْ سنن ابوداود، بَابٌ فِي الْإِمَامِ يَسْتَأْثِرُ بِشَيْءٍ مِنَ القَيْءِ لِنَفْسِهِ، نمبر 2755)
٢٨ وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَإِذَا لَمْ يَجْعَلْ السَّلَبَ لِلْقَاتِلِ \ عَنْ أَبِي قَتَادَةَ هِ قَالَ: «خَرَجْنَا مَعَ رَسُولِ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم عَامَ حُنَيْنٍ، ..... وَجَلَسَ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَقَالَ: مَنْ قَتَلَ قَتِيلًا لَهُ عَلَيْهِ بَيِّنَةٌ فَلَهُ سَلَبُهُ فَقُمْتُ فَقُلْتُ: مَنْ يَشْهَدُ لي، ثُمَّ جَلَسْتُ ثُمَّ قَالَ: مَنْ قَتَلَ قَتِيلًا لَهُ عَلَيْهِ بَيْنَةٌ فَلَهُ سَلَبُهُ، فَقُمْتُ فَقُلْتُ: مَنْ يَشْهَدُ لِي (صحيح البخاري بَابُ مَنْ لَمْ يُخَمسِ الْأَسْلَابَ، نمبر 3142) وجه: (٢) الحديث لثبوت وَإِذَا لَمْ يَجْعَلْ السَّلَبَ لِلْقَاتِلِ \ فَقَالَ أَبُو بَكْرِ الصِّدِّيقُ : لَاهَا اللَّهِ، اصول : اگر امام با ضابطہ کسی خاص دشمن کے قتل کرنے پر انعام مقرر کرے تو ایسے مقتول پر انعام کا مستحق ہو گا
Book of Siyar. 25: There is no harm for the Imam to give extra reward (yanfil) during battle and to encourage killing with the extra reward, saying: 'Whoever kills a slain person, his belongings (salab) are for him.' 26: And he says to the detachment: 'I have given you the quarter after the fifth.' And he does not give extra reward after the booty has been secured in Dar al-Islam except from the fifth. 28: And if he does not assign the salab to the killer, then it is part of the general booty, and the killer and others are equal in it. Proof 1: The verse... etc.
Source pages p. 378

Commentary
This passage from Al-Quduri's Mukhtasar presents rulings on tanfil (extra reward from spoils) during jihad. The Hanafi position is that the Imam may promise extra rewards to soldiers during battle to encourage fighting. This is permissible (la ba's). The Prophet ﷺ used to say, 'Whoever kills an enemy, his salab (weapons, clothes, mount) is for him.' The Imam may also tell a detachment that they will receive a quarter of the booty after the khums is taken. However, the Imam cannot give such extra rewards after the booty has been brought to Dar al-Islam and secured; then he can only give from the khums (the fifth portion). The second ruling clarifies that if the Imam does not specifically assign the salab to the killer, then it becomes part of the general booty to be distributed among all soldiers equally. The proofs cited include the Quranic verse (Al-Anfal 8:65) about encouraging believers, and hadith from Abu Qatada and others showing the Prophet's practice.

Key Terms
النَّفْل (al-nafl): Extra reward or additional spoils given by the Imam to soldiers beyond the regular share, as an incentive.
السَّلَب (al-salab): The belongings of a slain enemy, including clothes, weapons, and mount, which may be given to the killer as a reward.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on an Imam promising extra spoils (tanfil) after the booty has been secured in Dar al-Islam?
A) Permissible from the general booty.
B) Permissible only from the khums.
C) Not permissible at all.
D) Permissible if the promise was made before the battle.

Key Takeaway
The Imam may grant extra rewards during battle, but after the booty is secured, he may only give from the khums; otherwise, unassigned spoils are shared equally.

Definition of Salab and Ruling on Using Booty in Dar al-Harb
Defines salab and prohibits premature use of booty

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of salab and apply the prohibition on using booty while still in Dar al-Harb.

Core Idea
Salab is only what the slain enemy wears or rides; booty cannot be used until distributed after leaving enemy territory.

This lesson explains two interrelated rulings from the Hanafi school on military expeditions. First, what exactly constitutes the salab (spoils taken directly from a slain enemy). Second, the strict prohibition on consuming or using any part of the general booty (ghanimah) while the army remains in Dar al-Harb. Understanding these rules ensures that warriors and commanders respect the collective ownership of booty before official division.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of salab
The text defines salab as 'what is on the slain person from his clothes, his weapons, and his mount.' This includes anything carried on his person or mounted, but not other property like money or goods.
The definition is lexically precise: 'ma 'ala al-maqtul' restricts it to items physically on the slain.
2
Note the proof for the definition
The author cites multiple hadith, notably the Prophet giving the sword of Abu Jahl to Ibn Mas'ud, showing that weapons are part of salab. Another hadith shows horses and equipment being given as salab.
These are ahad hadith, but their multiple chains strengthen the ruling.
3
Understand the prohibition on using booty
The text states that when Muslims leave Dar al-Harb, they may not feed animals or eat from the booty. Any leftover fodder or food must be returned to the common pool.
This applies to ghanimah, not salab (which belongs to the killer immediately).
4
Recognize the rationale
Booty is collective property until officially divided by the Imam. Using it prematurely violates the rights of other participants and the shares due to Allah (khums).
The prohibition is derived from general principles and specific practices of the Companions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القدوري مع احاديثه 379
كِتَابُ السّير
وَالسَّلَبُ مَا عَلَى الْمَقْتُولِ مِنْ ثِيَابِهِ وَسِلَاحِهِ وَمَرْكَبِهِ
٣٠ وَإِذَا خَرَجَ الْمُسْلِمُونَ مِنْ دَارِ الْحَرْبِ لَمَّ يَجْرُ أَنْ يَعْلِفُوا مِنْ الْغَنِيمَةِ وَلَا يَأْكُلُوا مِنْهَا شَيْئًا وَمَنْ فَضَلَ مَعَهُ عَلَفٌ أَوْ طَعَامٌ رَدَّهُ إِلَى الْغَنِيمَةِ
وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَالسَّلَبُ مَا عَلَى الْمَقْتُولِ مِنْ ثِيَابِهِ عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْن مَسْعُودٍ، قَالَ: «نَفَّلَنِي رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم يَوْمَ بَدْرٍ سَيْفَ أَبِي جَهْلِ كَانَ قَتَلَهُ» (سنن ابوداود، بَابُ مَنْ أَجَازَ عَلَى جَرِيح مُنْخَنِ يُنَفَّلُ مِنْ سَلَبِهِ، غير 2722)
وجه : (۲) الحديث لثبوت وَالسَّلَبُ مَا عَلَى الْمَقْتُولِ مِنْ ثِيَابِهِ عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ، قَالَ: «بَعَثَنَا رَسُولُ الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فِي سَرِيَّةٍ فَبَلَغَتْ سُهْمَانُنَا التي عَشَرَ بَعِيرًا، وَنَفَّلَنَا رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم بَعِيرًا بَعِيرًا» (سنن ابوداود ، بَابٌ فِي نَفْلِ السَّرِيَّةِ تَخْرُجُ مِنَ الْعَسْكَر ، غبر 2745)
وجه : (۳) الحديث لثبوت وَالسَّلَبُ مَا عَلَى الْمَقْتُولِ مِنْ ثِيَابِهِ أَنَّ مَدَدِيَّا رَافَقَهُمْ فِي غَزْوَةِ مُؤْتَةَ ، وَأَنَّ رُومِيًّا كَانَ يَشُدُّ عَلَى الْمُسْلِمِينَ وَيُغْرِي بِهِمْ ، فَتَلَطَّفَ لَهُ ذَلِكَ الْمَدَدِيُّ ، فَأَقْبَل بِفَرَسِهِ ، وَسَيْفِهِ ، وَسَرْجِهِ ، وَلَجَامِهِ ، وَمِنْطَقَتِهِ ، وَسِلَاحِهِ ، كُلُّ ذَلِكَ مُذَهَبٌ بِالذَّهَبِ وَالْجُوْهَرِ ، إِلَى خَالِدِ بْنِ الْوَلِيدِ ، فَأَخَذَ مِنْهُ خَالِدٌ طَائِفَةً ، وَنَفَّلَهُ بَقِيَّتَهُ ، فَقُلْتُ: يَا خَالِدُ ، مَا هَذَا؟ أَمَا تَعْلَمُ أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم نَفَّلَ الْقَاتِلَ السَّلَبَ كُلَّهُ ، قَالَ بَلَى ، وَلَكِنِّي اسْتَكْثَرْتُهُ (شرح معاني الآثار، بَابُ الرَّجُل يَقْتُلُ قَتِيلًا فِي دَارِ الْحَرْبِ ، هَلْ يَكُونُ لَهُ سَلْبُهُ أَمْ لَا ، غبر 5206)
وجه : (۱) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَالسَّلَبُ مَا عَلَى الْمَقْتُولِ مِنْ ثِيَابِهِ فَكَتَبَ إِلَيَّ عُمَرُأَنْ دَعِ النَّاسَ يَأْكُلُونَ وَيَعْلِفُونَ ، فَمَنْ بَاعَ شَيْئًا بِذَهَبٍ، أَوْ فِضَّةٍ، فَقَدْ وَجَبَ فِيهِ خُمْسُ اللَّهِ، وَسِهَامُ الْمُسْلِمِينَ» (مصنف ابن شيبه في الطَّعَامِ وَالْعَلَفِ يُؤْخَذُ مِنْهُ الشَّيْءُ فِي أَرْضِ الْعَدُوّ ، نمبر 33330) د. وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَإِذَا خَرَجَ الْمُسْلِمُونَ مِنْ دَارِ الْحَرْبِ فَقَالَ مُعَادٌ: «غَزَوْنَا مَعَ رَسُولِ اصول : سلب میں مقتول کا ہتھیار ، مقتول کا کپڑا، مقتول کی سواری، لگام اور اس پر لگی بڑی تھیلی اور اس تھیلی میں جو کچھ سامان موجود ہو وہ سب سلب میں شامل ہے اس کے علاوہ چیزیں سلب میں شامل نہیں ہیں۔
Al-Quduri with his hadiths 379. Book of Siyar. And the salab is what is on the slain person from his clothes, his weapons, and his mount. And when the Muslims leave Dar al-Harb, it is not permissible for them to feed (their animals) from the booty nor to eat from it anything. And whoever has leftover fodder or food, he must return it to the booty. Proof 1: Hadith from Abdullah ibn Mas'ud... etc.
Source pages p. 379

Commentary
This lesson defines salab and gives a rule about booty when leaving enemy territory. The Hanafi definition: salab includes the slain enemy's clothes, weapons, and mount (including saddle, reins, etc.). It does not include other possessions like money or goods not on his person. The hadith show that the Prophet gave the sword of Abu Jahl to the killer, and that he gave extra camels. The ruling also prohibits Muslims from using any part of the booty for fodder or food while still in Dar al-Harb, and leftover must be returned to the common pool. Proofs include the practice of Umar and a hadith from Mu'adh.

Key Terms
السَّلَب (al-salab): The belongings of a slain enemy: his clothes, weapons, and mount.
دَار الْحَرْب (dar al-harb): Territory under non-Muslim control where the rulings of jihad apply.
الْغَنِيمَة (al-ghanimah): Booty captured from the enemy, excluding salab.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on using captured booty for fodder while still in Dar al-Harb?
A) Permissible (mubah)
B) Recommended (mandub)
C) Prohibited (haram)
D) Neutral (ja'iz)

Key Takeaway
Salab is limited to the slain enemy's combat gear; any use of general booty before leaving enemy territory is prohibited.

Entitlement to Shares and Radkh in Spoils
Ruling with proof from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rules on who receives fixed shares of ghanimah and who receives radkh, and apply the principle that share is determined at time of entry into battle.

Core Idea
Fixed shares belong only to free Muslim male combatants; others receive radkh at the Imam's discretion.

This passage from Kitab al-Siyar clarifies the distribution of spoils (ghanimah) in Hanafi fiqh. The central principle is that entitlement to a fixed share (sahm) is determined by one's status at the moment of entering the battlefield, not by later changes. The text then enumerates categories of people who do not receive shares—slaves, women, children, the insane, and dhimmis—and explains that the Imam may give them a discretionary gift (radkh). We will examine the ruling, its proof from hadith, and the rationale behind the distinction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its conditions
The passage states two rulings: (1) the share is fixed at entry; (2) certain persons get radkh, not shares. Identify each act and its hukm.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The author cites the hadith of Ibn Abbas (narrated by Muslim) about women and slaves, and the hadith about the Prophet granting radkh to the Jews of Banu Qaynuqa'. Note the chain and the specific words used.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (legal inference)
Explain how the phrase 'ليس لهما شيء إلا أن يحذيا' proves that radkh is not a fixed right but a discretionary gift. Also, the absence of a share for non-combatants is derived from the negation of a share.
4
Note the scope and ikhtilaf
The Hanafi position is that shares are only for free Muslim male combatants. Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may give a share to women if they actively fight. Understand the difference and its practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
A man enters the battlefield on foot, then buys a horse. According to the rule, he receives the foot soldier's share because the entitlement is determined at entry. Confirm the logic.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ السّير
وَمَنْ دَخَلَ رَاجِلًا فَاشْتَرَى فَرَسًا اسْتَحَقَّ سَهْمَ رَاجِلِ وَلَا يُسْهَمُ لِمَمْلُوكِ وَلَا امْرَأَةٍ وَلَا صَيَ وَلَا تَجَنُونٍ وَلَا ذِمِّي وَلَكِنْ يَرْضَخُ هُمُ الْإِمَامُ عَلَى قَدْرِ مَا يَرَى
وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَمَنْ دَخَلَ دَارَ الْحَرْبِ فَارِسًا فَنَفَقَ فَرَسُهُ اسْتَحَقَّ سَهْمَ كَتَبَ تَجْدَةُ بْنُ عَامِرٍ الْحَرُورِيُّ إِلَى ابْنِ عَبَّاسِ يَسْأَلُهُ عَنِ الْعَبْدِ وَالْمَرْأَةِ يَحْضُرَانِ الْمَعْلَمَ، هَلْ يُقْسَمُ فَهُمَا؟ فَلَوْلَا أَنْ يَقَعَ فِي أُخْمُوقَةٍ مَا كَتَبْتُ إِلَيْهِ. اكْتُبْ إِنَّكَ كَتَبْتَ تَسْأَلُنِي عَنِ الْمَرْأَةِ وَالْعَبْدِ يَحْضُرَانِ الْمَغْنَمَ، هَلْ يُقْسَمُ فَهُمَا شَيْءٌ؟ وَإِنَّهُ لَيْسَ لَهُمَا شَيْءٌ إِلَّا أَنْ يُحْذَيَا(مسلم شريف، بَاب النِّسَاءِ الْغَازِيَاتِ يُرْضَخُ فَهُنَّ وَلَا يُسْهَمُ. وَالنَّهْيِ عَنْ قَتْلِ صِبْيَانِ أَهْلِ الْحَرْبِ،نمبر 1812)
وجه:(۲) الحديث لثبوت وَمَنْ دَخَلَ دَارَ الْخَرْبِ فَارِسًا فَنَفَقَ فَرَسُهُ عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ رضي اللَّه عنهما ، أَنَّهُ قَالَ : اسْتَعَاذَنَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم بِيَهُودِ بَنِي قَيْنُقَاعَ فَرَضَحَ لَهُمْ، وَلَمْ يُسْهِمْ لَهُمْ (الكبري الدُّنْيَا للبيهقي، بَابُ الرَّضْحُ لِمَنْ يُسْتَعَانُ بِهِ مِنْ أَهْلِ الذِمَّةِ عَلَى قِتَالِ الْمُشْرِكِينَ، غبر 17970)
Book of Siyar. And whoever entered on foot then bought a horse, he deserves the share of a foot soldier. And no share is given to a slave, nor a woman, nor a child, nor a insane person, nor a dhimmi, but the Imam gives them a radkh (gratuity) according to what he sees. [Hadith for proof of: And whoever entered the abode of war as a cavalryman then his horse died, he deserves the share of a cavalryman; Najda ibn Amir al-Haruri wrote to Ibn Abbas asking about the slave and woman attending the battle, whether a share is given to them? He replied: You wrote to me asking about the woman and slave attending the spoils, whether anything is divided for them? They have nothing except that they may be given a radkh (Muslim, chapter on women fighters, they are given radkh and not shares, and prohibition of killing children of enemy, no. 1812). [Hadith for proof of: And whoever entered the abode of war as a cavalryman then his horse died; from Ibn Abbas that the Prophet sought help from Jews of Banu Qaynuqa' and gave them radkh and did not give them a share (al-Bayhaqi? no. 17970).
Source pages p. 382

Commentary
This passage from Kitab al-Siyar states rulings on entitlement to shares of spoils (ghanimah). The author first addresses a scenario: a person enters the battlefield on foot, then later buys a horse. He still gets the share of a foot soldier, not a cavalryman, because the share is determined by his status at the time of entering the battle. Then general rules: no fixed share is given to slaves, women, children, the insane, or dhimmis (non-Muslim subjects). However, the Imam may grant them a discretionary radkh (gratuity) based on their contribution and his judgment. The supporting hadiths confirm that women and slaves receive radkh, not shares, as per the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) in the conquest of Khaibar and other battles. Another hadith shows that even when the Prophet sought help from Jews (dhimmis), they were given radkh, not shares. This highlights the Hanafi principle that fixed shares are only for free Muslim male combatants; others may be compensated at the Imam's discretion.

Key Terms
السَّهْم (al-sahm): A fixed share of the spoils (ghanimah) given to eligible combatants.
الرَّضْخ (al-radhkh): A discretionary gratuity given by the Imam to those who are not entitled to fixed shares of spoils (like women, slaves, dhimmis).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, a dhimmi who fights alongside Muslims in a battle:
A) Receives a full share like a Muslim soldier
B) Receives half a share
C) Receives no share but may be given radkh by the Imam
D) Receives nothing at all, not even radkh

Key Takeaway
Fixed shares of spoils are only for free Muslim male combatants, determined at time of entry; all others receive only a discretionary radkh from the Imam.

Khums After the Prophet: Three Shares Only
Ruling on khums shares after Prophet's death

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the distribution of khums after the Prophet's death and identify the proofs that the Prophet's share and relatives' share lapsed.

Core Idea
The Prophet's share and relatives' share in khums lapsed with his death; only three shares remain.

The khums (one-fifth of spoils) had a specific allocation during the Prophet's lifetime, including shares for him and his relatives. This lesson examines the Hanafi view that these shares ceased after his death, based on explicit hadith and the practice of the Companions. Understanding this shift is essential for correct application of khums rulings today.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
Determine the act (distribution of khums) and its legal classification after the Prophet's death. The text states it is divided into three shares, and the Prophet's share and relatives' share have lapsed.
The ruling is for the post-Prophetic era; during his life, there were five shares.
2
Examine the primary proof
Read the hadith from Abu Hurairah: 'My heirs do not divide a dinar; what I leave after the maintenance of my wives and my worker is charity.' This shows the Prophet's personal share is not inherited and thus lapses.
Also the hadith on safiy (special choice) lapses with his death.
3
Analyze the proof for relatives' share
The hadith from Ali and Jubair ibn Mut'im show that the relatives' share was tied to support (nusra) during the Prophet's life; after him, it is only given to poor relatives, subsumed under the needy category.
Thus the relatives' share as a separate category lapses.
4
Contrast with other schools
The Shafi'i school holds that khums continues in five shares, with the Prophet's share going to the caliph and the relatives' share remaining a distinct category. Identify the basis of their view.
The Hanafi response: after the Prophet, no one stands in his place for the personal share, and the relatives' share was conditional on nusra.
5
Apply the Hanafi ruling
The khums is now wajib to distribute to three categories: orphans, needy (including poor relatives), and travelers. Ensure rich relatives receive nothing.
The poor relatives are given priority over other needy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَأَمَّا الْخُمْسُ فَيُقَسَّمُ عَلَى ثَلَاثَةِ أَسْهُم سَهُمْ لِلْيَتَامَى وَسَهُمْ لِلْمَسَاكِينِ وَسَهُمْ لِأَبْنَاءِ السَّبِيلِ... وَيَدْخُلُ فُقَرَاءُ ذَوِي الْقُرْبَى فِيهِمْ وَيُقَدَّمُونَ وَلَا يَدْفَعُ إِلَى أَغْنِيَائِهِمْ شَيْئًا فَأَمَّا مَا ذَكَرَهُ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى لِنَفْسِهِ فِي كِتَابِهِ مِنْ الْخَمْسِ فَإِنَّمَا هُوَ لِافْتِتَاحِ الْكَلَامِ تَبَرِّكًا بِاسْمِهِ تَعَالَى وَسَهْمُ النَّبِيِّ - صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ - سَقَطَ بِمَوْتِهِ كَمَا سَقَطَ الصَّفِيُّ وَسَهُمُ ذَوِي الْقُرْبَى كَانُوا يَسْتَحِقُونَهُ فِي زَمَنِ النَّبِيِّ - صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ - بِالنُّصْرَةِ وَبَعْدَهُ بِالْفَقْرِ
وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت فَأَمَّا الْخُمْسُ فَيُقَسَّمُ عَلَى ثَلَاثَةِ أَسْهُمْ سَأَلْتُ الْحَسَنَ بْنَ مُحَمَّدٍ عَنْ قَوْلِ الله تبارك وتعالى {وَاعْلَمُوا أَنَّمَا غَنِمْتُمْ مِنْ شَيْءٍ فَأَنَّ لِلَّهِ خُمُسَهُ وَلِلرَّسُولِ} [الأنفال: 41] الْآيَةُ. فَقَالَ: «هَذَا مِفْتَاحُ كَلَامِ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى مَا فِي الدُّنْيَا وَالْآخِرَةِ» (المستدرك علي الصحيحين للحاكم، والأصل من كتاب الله عز وجل، نمبر 2585)
وجه: (٢) الحديث لثبوت فَأَمَّا الْخُمْسُ فَيُقَسَّمُ عَلَى ثَلَاثَةِ أَسْهُم عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ : أَنَّ رَسُولَ الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «لَا يَقْتَسِمُ وَرَثَتِي دِينَارًا، مَا تَرَكْتُ بَعْدَ نَفَقَةِ نِسَائِي وَمَؤُونَةِ عَامِلِي فَهُوَ صَدَقَةٌ.» (صحيح البخاري ، بَابُ نَفَقَةِ نِسَاءِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم بَعْدَ وَفَاتِهِ، نمبر 3096)
ود وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَيَدْخُلُ فُقَرَاءُ ذَوِي الْقُرْبَى فِيهِمْ سَمِعْتُ عَلِيًّا، يَقُولُ: «وَلَّاتِي رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم خَمُسَ الْخُمُسِ»، فَوَضَعْتُهُ مَوَاضِعَهُ حَيَاةَ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم وَحَيَاةَ أَبِي بَكْرٍ، وَحَيَاةَ عُمَرَ، فَأَتِي بِمَالٍ فَدَعَانِي فَقَالَ: خُذْهُ، فَقُلْتُ لا أريدُهُ، قَالَ: خُذْهُ فَأَنْتُمْ أَحَقُّ بِهِ، قُلْتُ: قَدِ اسْتَغْنَيْنَا عَنْهُ فَجَعَلَهُ فِي بَيْتِ الْمَالِ" (سنن ابوداود، بَابٌ فِي بَيَانِ مَوَاضِعِ قَسْمِ الْخُمُسِ، وَسَهْمِ ذِي الْقُرْبَى، غير (2983)
٢٠ وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت فَأَمَّا مَا ذَكَرَهُ اللهُ تَعَالَى لِنَفْسِهِ سَأَلْتُ الْحَسَنَ بْنَ مُحَمَّدٍ عَنْ قَوْلِ اللَّهِ تبارك وتعالى {وَاعْلَمُوا أَنَّمَا غَنِمْتُمْ مِنْ شَيْءٍ فَأَنَّ لِلَّهِ خُمُسَهُ وَلِلرَّسُولِ} [الأنفال: 41] الْآيَةُ. فَقَالَ: «هَذَا مِفْتَاحُ كَلَامِ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى مَا فِي الدُّنْيَا وَالْآخِرَةِ» (المستدرك علي الصحيحين للحاكم، والأصل من كتاب الله عز وجل،نمبر2585)
الوجه: (ا) الحديث لثبوت وَسَهُمُ النَّبِيِّ - صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ عَنْ عَامِرِ الشَّعْبِيِّ، قَالَ: «كَانَ للنَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم سَهُمْ يُدْعَى الصَّفِيَّ، إِنْ شَاءَ عَبْدًا، وَإِنْ شَاءَ أَمَةً، وَإِنْ شَاءَ فَرَسًا يَخْتَارُهُ قَبْلَ الْخُمُسِ» (سنن ابوداود، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي سَهْمِ الصَّفِيِّ،نمبر 2991)
وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَسَهْمُ ذَوِي الْقُرْبَى كَانُوا يَسْتَحِقُونَهُ فِي زَمَنِ النَّبِيَا أَخْبَرَنِي جُبَيْرُ بْنُ مُطْعِمٍ، قَالَ: لَمَّا كَانَ يَوْمُ خَيْبَرَ وَضَعَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم سَهْمَ ذِي الْقُرْبَى فِي بَنِي هَاشِمٍ، وَبَنِي الْمُطَّلِبِ، وَتَرَكَ بَنِي نَوْفَلِ، وَبَنِي عَبْدِ شَمْسٍ فَانْطَلَقْتُ أَنَا وَعُثْمَانُ بْنُ عَفَّانَ حَتَّى أَتَيْنَا النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم، فَقُلْنَا: يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ، هَؤُلَاءِ بَنُو هَاشِمٍ لَا تُنْكِرُ فَضْلَهُمْ لِلْمَوْضِعِ الَّذِي وَضَعَكَ
As for the khums, it is divided into three shares: a share for orphans, a share for the needy, and a share for travelers. And the poor of the near relatives are included among them and given priority, and nothing is given to their rich. As for what Allah mentioned for Himself in His book of the khums, that is only for opening the speech, seeking blessing from His name. And the share of the Prophet (peace be upon him) has lapsed with his death, just as the safiy (special choice) lapsed. And the share of the near relatives: they used to deserve it in the time of the Prophet (peace be upon him) through support (nusra), and after him through poverty.
[The hadith references follow]
Source pages p. 382

Commentary
This passage explains the distribution of khums after the death of the Prophet (peace be upon him). Originally, khums was divided into five shares: Allah's (opening phrase), the Prophet's, relatives, orphans, needy, and travelers. After the Prophet's death, his share and the relatives' share are discontinued. The khums is now only three shares: orphans, needy, and travelers. Within this, poor relatives (dhawi al-qurba) are included and given priority over others, but rich relatives receive nothing. The hadiths support this: one from al-Hasan ibn Muhammad explains that the mention of Allah's share is just an opening blessing, not an actual share. Another hadith from Abu Huraira states that the Prophet's heirs do not inherit his wealth; it is charity. The hadith from Ali shows that he managed the khums and eventually placed the surplus in the treasury. The hadith from Jubair ibn Mut'im shows that the Prophet allocated the relatives' share to Banu Hashim and Banu al-Muttalib, excluding others. Thus, the Hanafi position is that after the Prophet's death, the khums is distributed to three categories, and the relatives' share is not a separate entitlement but is subsumed under these if they are poor.

Key Terms
الخُمْس (al-khums): One-fifth of the spoils of war, which is set aside for specific recipients as prescribed in the Quran.
الصَّفِيُّ (al-saffiyy): A special choice the Prophet had to select any item from the spoils before division, which also lapsed with his death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
After the death of the Prophet (peace be upon him), what happens to the share of khums that was for the Prophet and his relatives?
A) It continues to be given to the caliph and relatives
B) It lapses, and khums is divided into three shares only
C) It is given exclusively to the Banu Hashim
D) It is distributed equally among all Muslims

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school teaches that after the Prophet's death, khums is distributed to only three categories: orphans, needy (including poor relatives), and travelers.

intermediate

The Hanafi Ruling on Fay': Public Welfare, Not Spoils
Ruling with proofs for fay'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on fay' and distinguish it from ghanimah by citing the Quranic verse and two hadiths.

Core Idea
Fay' is public trust, not war spoils; it must be spent on Muslim interests.

You know that war booty (ghanimah) captured by force is divided among the fighters. But what about property obtained without a battle—through a peace treaty or tribute? Classical scholars called this fay', and the Hanafi school holds a distinct position: it belongs to the entire community, to be spent on public welfare. In this lesson, you will examine the primary evidences that separate fay' from ghanimah and see how the Hanafi school derives its ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage states: property taken from the enemy without fighting (fay') is to be spent on the interests of the Muslims, just like kharaj (land tax). This is the operative ruling.
Fay' includes tribute, jizyah from peace treaties, and land surrendered without war.
2
Locate the first evidence: the Quranic verse
Surah al-Hashr (59:7) lists the recipients of fay' from towns: Allah, the Messenger, relatives, orphans, the needy, and the traveler. Notably absent are the fighters who participated in battle.
The verse does not mention a four-fifths share for soldiers, contrasting with ghanimah distribution.
3
Analyze the hadiths on conquest and peace
Two hadiths are cited: (1) Abu Hurairah reports that towns conquered without force belong to Allah and His Messenger (i.e., public treasury), while towns taken by force have one-fifth for Allah and the Messenger and the rest for fighters. (2) The peace treaty of Najran shows that tribute from a non-war situation goes to the Muslims collectively.
The first hadith draws a clear line between fay' and ghanimah. The second exemplifies fay' in practice.
4
Note the statement of Sufyan al-Thawri
The Tabi'i explicitly distinguishes fay' from ghanimah: ghanimah is taken by force and divided (four-fifths to fighters), while fay' results from peace and is entirely at the imam's disposal for public welfare.
This early authority supports the Hanafi position.
5
Recognize the cross-madhhab dispute
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that fay' is divided like ghanimah, with four-fifths for fighters. The Hanafi position relies on the Quranic verse and the hadith to argue otherwise. The practical difference: under Shafi'i, soldiers get a share of tribute; under Hanafi, the entire amount goes to state welfare.
The evidence for the Hanafi view is considered qat'i in thubut and dalalah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ السّير
وَمَا أَوْجَفَ عَلَيْهِ الْمُسْلِمُونَ مِنْ أَمْوَالِ أَهْلِ الْحَرْبِ بِغَيْرِ قِتَالٍ صُرِفَ فِي مَصَالِحِ الْمُسْلِمِينَ كَمَا يُصْرَفُ الخَرَاجُ. خَيْبَرَ، فَغَلَبَ عَلَى النَّخْلِ وَالْأَرْضِ... فَوَجَدُوا الْمَسْكَ، فَقَتَلَ ابْنَ أَبِي الْحَقِيقِ [؟] وَسَبَيَ نِسَاءَهُمْ وَذَرَارِيَّهُمْ. (سنن أبي داود بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي حُكْمِ أَرْضِ خَيْبَرَ، رقم 3006)

وَجه: (١) قول التابعي: عَنِ الثَّوْرِيِّ قَالَ: "الْفَيْءُ وَالْغَنِيمَةُ مُخْتَلِفَانِ، أَمَّا الْغَنِيمَةُ: فَمَا أَخَذَ الْمُسْلِمُونَ فَصَارَ فِي أَيْدِيهِمْ مِنَ الْكُفَّارِ، وَالْخَمْسُ فِي ذَلِكَ إِلَى الْأَمِيرِ يَضَعُهُ حَيْثُمَا أَمَرَ اللَّهُ، وَالْأَرْبَعَةُ الْأَخْمَاسِ الْبَاقِيَةُ لِلَّذِينَ غَنِمُوا الْغَنِيمَةَ، وَالْفَيْءُ: مَا وَقَعَ مِنْ صُلْحٍ بَيْنَ الْإِمَامِ وَالْكُفَّارِ فِي أَعْنَاقِهِمْ، وَأَرْضِهِمْ، وَزَرْعِهِمْ، وَفِيمَا صُولِحُوا عَلَيْهِ مِمَّا لَمْ يَأْخُذْهُ الْمُسْلِمُونَ عَنْوَةً، وَلَمْ يَحُوزُوهُ، وَلَمْ يَقْهَرُوهُ عَلَيْهِ، حَتَّى وَقَعَ فِيهِ بَيْنَهُمْ صُلْحٌ" قَالَ: «فَذَلِكَ الصُّلْحُ إِلَى الْإِمَامِ، يَضَعُهُ حَيْثُ أَمَرَ اللَّهُ». (مصنف عبد الرزاق، بَابُ الْغَنِيمَةِ وَالْفَيْءِ مُخْتَلِفَانِ، رقم 9778)

وَجه: (٢) الآية: {مَا أَفَاءَ اللَّهُ عَلَى رَسُولِهِ مِنْ أَهْلِ الْقُرَى فَلِلَّهِ وَلِلرَّسُولِ وَلِذِي الْقُرْبَى وَالْيَتَامَى وَالْمَسَاكِينِ وَابْنِ السَّبِيلِ} (سورة الحشر: ٧)

وَجه: (٣) الحديث: عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ ﷺ قَالَ: "أَيُّمَا قَرْيَةٍ افْتَتَحَهَا اللهُ وَرَسُولُهُ فَهِيَ لِلَّهِ وَلِرَسُولِهِ، وَأَيُّمَا قَرْيَةٍ افْتَتَحَهَا الْمُسْلِمُونَ عَنْوَةً فَخُمُسُهَا لِلَّهِ وَلِرَسُولِهِ وَبَقِيَّتُهَا لِمَنْ قَاتَلَ عَلَيْهَا". (سنن البيهقي، بَابُ مَنْ رَأَى قِسْمَةَ الْأَرَاضِي الْمَغْنُومَةِ، رقم 18393)

وَجه: (٤) الحديث: عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ قَالَ: «صَالَحَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ أَهْلَ نَجْرَانَ عَلَى أَلْفَيْ حُلَّةٍ، النِّصْفُ فِي صَفَرٍ، وَالْبَقِيَّةُ فِي رَجَبٍ، يُؤَدُّونَهَا إِلَى الْمُسْلِمِينَ». (سنن أبي داود، بَابٌ فِي أَخْذِ الجِزْيَةِ، رقم 3041)

اصول: مال فئی جو قتال کے بغیر دشمن سے ملے وہ بیت المال میں جمع ہو کر مصلحت امت پر خرچ ہو گا۔
Book of Siyar. And what the Muslims take from the wealth of the people of war without fighting is spent on the interests of the Muslims, just as the kharaj is spent. Khaybar: they overcame the date palms and land... they found the musk, killed Ibn Abi al-Haqiq, and captured their women and children. (Sunan Abi Dawud, chapter on the ruling of the land of Khaybar, no. 3006) Evidence (1): Statement of the Tabi'i: al-Thawri said: 'Fay' and ghanimah are different. As for ghanimah: it is what the Muslims take from the disbelievers and it comes into their possession; one-fifth of that goes to the ruler to place as Allah commanded, and the remaining four-fifths are for those who gained the ghanimah. As for fay': it is what occurs from a peace treaty between the imam and the disbelievers concerning their persons, lands, and crops, and regarding what they made peace upon, which the Muslims did not take by force, did not seize, and did not overcome, until a peace treaty occurred between them.' He said: 'That peace treaty is for the imam to place as Allah commanded.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, chapter on ghanimah and fay' being different, no. 9778) Evidence (2): The verse: {What Allah restored to His Messenger from the people of the towns, it is for Allah and for the Messenger and for the relatives and the orphans and the needy and the traveler} (Surah al-Hashr: 7). Evidence (3): The hadeeth: From Abu Hurairah that the Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: 'Any town that Allah and His Messenger conquer, it is for Allah and His Messenger. And any town that the Muslims conquer by force, one-fifth is for Allah and His Messenger, and the remainder is for those who fought for it.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter on those who held dividing conquered lands, no. 18393) Evidence (4): The hadeeth: From Ibn Abbas who said: 'The Messenger of Allah ﷺ made peace with the people of Najran for two thousand garments, half in Safar and the remainder in Rajab, which they would pay to the Muslims.' (Sunan Abi Dawud, chapter on taking jizyah, no. 3041) Principle: Wealth from fay' that is obtained from the enemy without fighting is collected in the bayt al-mal and spent on the welfare of the ummah.
Source pages p. 387

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from Kitab al-Siyar dealing with property acquired from the enemy without actual fighting, known as fay'. The author begins by stating the ruling: such property is spent on the interests (masalih) of the Muslims, just like kharaj revenue. He then provides evidence (wujuh). First, he quotes Sufyan al-Thawri, who distinguishes between ghanimah (spoils taken by force) and fay' (property obtained by peace treaty). In ghanimah, four-fifths go to the fighters and one-fifth to the ruler for public expenditure. In fay', the entire amount is at the imam's discretion for public welfare, as the Muslims did not risk their lives to obtain it. Then the author cites Quranic verse 59:7, which instructs that fay' from towns be distributed to specific categories, indicating it is not for the fighters alone. Next, a hadith from Abu Hurairah explicitly states that towns conquered without force belong to Allah and His Messenger (i.e., the public treasury), while those conquered by force have one-fifth for the ruler and four-fifths for the fighters. Finally, a hadith about the peace treaty of Najran shows that tribute from peaceful agreements goes to the Muslims collectively, not divided as spoils. The Urdu note summarizes: fay' is collected in the treasury and spent on the ummah's welfare.

Key Terms
الفيء (al-fay'): Property obtained from the enemy without fighting, e.g., through peace treaty or tribute.
الغنيمة (al-ghanimah): Spoils taken from the enemy by force of arms.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on property obtained from the enemy without fighting (fay')?
A) It is distributed as ghanimah among the fighters.
B) It is spent on the interests of the Muslims.
C) It belongs to the Imam personally.
D) It is returned to the enemy.

Key Takeaway
Fay' is a public trust to be spent on the welfare of the entire Muslim community, not distributed as personal spoils of war.

Defining 'Ushr and Kharaj Lands in Hanafi Fiqh
Defining boundaries and ownership of 'ushr and kharaj lands.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the geographic boundaries of 'ushr and kharaj lands according to the Hanafi school and state the ruling on ownership of Sawad land.

Core Idea
Arab land pays 'ushr; Sawad pays kharaj, but both remain privately owned.

The early Islamic state distinguished between lands based on how they were conquered and administered. The Hanafi school, relying on the practice of Caliph 'Umar, defines two categories: 'ushr land (tithe) and kharaj land (land tax). This lesson from al-Quduri's matn specifies their exact boundaries and the ownership status of Sawad.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two land categories
Find ard al-'ushr and ard al-kharaj in the text and note their defining characteristics.
The passage explicitly names both categories.
2
Locate the geographic boundaries
For 'ushr land: from al-Udhayb to the farthest stone in Yemen to the border of Syria. For kharaj land: from al-Udhayb to Hulwan and from al-Alth to Abbadan.
These boundaries define the historical Sawad region.
3
Determine the ruling on ownership
The text states that the land of Sawad is owned by its people and that sale and disposal are permissible.
This is a key Hanafi ruling distinguishing tax status from ownership.
4
Note the legal significance
The classification determines tax rates (tithe vs. variable land tax) and legal capacity to transfer ownership.
Misclassification leads to incorrect fiscal obligations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ السّير فصل : ١ وَأَرْضُ الْعَرَبِ كُلُّهَا أَرْضُ عَشْرِ وَهِيَ مَا بَيْنَ الْعُذَيْبِ إِلَى أَقْصَى حَجَرٍ بِالْيَمَنِ بِمَهْرَةَ إِلَى حَدِ الشَّامِ . وَالسَّوَادُ كُلُّهَا أَرْضٌ خَرَاجٍ وَهِيَ مَا بَيْنَ الْعُذَيْبِ إِلَى عَقَبَةِ حُلْوَانَ وَمِنَ الْعَلْثِ إِلَى عَبَّادَانَ ، وَأَرْضُ السَّوَادِ كُلُّهَا مَمْلُوكَةٌ لِأَهْلِهَا يَجُوزُ بَيْعُهُمْ لَهَا وَتَصَرُّفُهُمْ فِيهَا
Book of Siyar: Section 1. All of the Arab land is 'ushr land, and it is what lies between al-Udhayb and the farthest stone in Yemen at Mahrah to the border of Syria. All of Sawad is kharaj land, and it is what lies between al-Udhayb and the pass of Hulwan and from al-Alth to Abbadan. All of the land of Sawad is owned by its people; their sale of it and their disposal of it are permissible.
Source pages p. 388

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the matn of al-Quduri defining two categories of land in the early Islamic state. The 'Arab land' (Jazirat al-Arab) is entirely 'ushr land, meaning it is subject to a tithe ('ushr) on agricultural produce. The boundaries given are from al-Udhayb (a place near Kufa) to the farthest part of Yemen and to Syria. In contrast, the Sawad (the fertile region of Iraq) is kharaj land, subject to a land tax (kharaj). The Sawad land remains privately owned by its inhabitants; they may sell and dispose of it freely. This ruling is based on the historical conquest of these areas and the policy of the early caliphs, particularly 'Umar ibn al-Khattab (RA). The Hanafi school maintains this distinction.

Key Terms
أرض العشر (ard al-'ushr): Land subject to a tithe of one-tenth of produce, applicable in the Arabian Peninsula.
أرض الخراج (ard al-kharaj): Land subject to a variable land tax (kharaj), applicable in the Sawad (Iraq).
السواد (al-sawad): The fertile agricultural region of Iraq extending from al-Udhayb to Hulwan and from al-Alth to Abbadan.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the classification of the land of Sawad (Iraq) according to this passage?
A) 'Ushr land, because it was conquered peacefully
B) Kharaj land, with ownership remaining with the original inhabitants
C) State-owned land subject to 'ushr
D) Land whose status depends on the religion of the cultivator

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school classifies land by geography: Arab land is 'ushr, Sawad is kharaj, and both are privately owned.

Land Classification: 'Ushr and Kharaj Based on Conquest or Conversion
Stating the tax ruling for land based on how it was acquired

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between 'ushr and kharaj lands according to the Hanafi school and apply the classification based on the method of acquisition.

Core Idea
The tax status of land is determined by how it was acquired: conversion, distribution, or leaving inhabitants.

This passage from al-Quduri provides a clear rule for classifying land as 'ushr or kharaj. The key factor is not the fertility but the circumstances of conquest or conversion. Understanding this distinction is essential for Islamic land law and its application in historical and contemporary contexts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios for land acquisition
The passage describes three possible origins: inhabitants converted to Islam while living on the land; land conquered by force and distributed among the troops; land conquered by force but inhabitants left in place. The first two result in 'ushr, the third in kharaj.
Note the distinction between distribution and leaving inhabitants.
2
Classify each scenario as 'ushr or kharaj
For conversion and conquest+distribution: 'ushr. For conquest+inhabitants remaining: kharaj.
3
Understand the legal principle
The Hanafi rule ties tax status to ownership: Muslim-owned land is 'ushr; land remaining under non-Muslim ownership (even under Muslim rule) is kharaj.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi agreement and cross-madhhab difference
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad agree. Shafi'is hold that conversion does not change land status if it was originally kharaj.
This is a key point of ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَكُلُّ أَرْضِ أَسْلَمَ أَهْلُهَا عَلَيْهَا أَوْ فُتِحَتْ عَنْوَةً وَقُسَمَتْ بَيْنَ الْغَانِمِينَ فَهِيَ أَرْضُ عُشْرٍ [ل؟] وَكُلُّ أَرْضِ فُتِحَتْ عَنْوَةً فَأَقِرَّ أَهْلُهَا عَلَيْهَا فَهِيَ أَرْضُ خَرَاجٍ
And every land whose inhabitants became Muslim upon it, or which was conquered by force and distributed among the spoils-takers, it is 'ushr land [؟]. And every land which was conquered by force and its inhabitants were left upon it, it is kharaj land.
Source pages p. 389

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from al-Quduri further categorizing lands based on the circumstances of conquest or conversion. It presents two rules: (1) If the inhabitants of a land become Muslim while still living on that land (i.e., they embrace Islam and retain their land), that land becomes 'ushr land; similarly, if a land is conquered by force (عنوة) and then distributed among the Muslim soldiers as spoils, it is 'ushr land. (2) If a land is conquered by force but the inhabitants are left in possession of their land (they are not expelled and the land is not distributed), it remains kharaj land. The underlying principle is that 'ushr applies to land owned by Muslims (whether by conversion or distribution), while kharaj applies to land remaining in the hands of non-Muslims under Muslim rule. The unclear word 'لَ' may be a scribal error for 'لا' affirming the 'ushr status, or it may be part of a phrase 'لا خراج عليها' (no kharaj on it). The relied-upon Hanafi position is as stated.

Key Terms
عَنْوَةً ('anwatan): By force, referring to conquest through military action.
قُسِمَتْ بَيْنَ الْغَانِمِينَ (qusimat bayna al-ghanimin): Distributed among the troops who participated in the conquest.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling for land conquered by force and distributed among the ghanimin?
A) Kharaj
B) 'Ushr
C) No tax
D) It depends on the fertility

Key Takeaway
The tax status of land in Hanafi law depends on how it was acquired: 'ushr for Muslim-owned land, kharaj for land remaining under non-Muslim ownership.

Abu Yusuf's View on Revived Land Classification
Intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Yusuf's rule and consensus on Basra

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Abu Yusuf's rule for classifying revived dead land and explain how the consensus on Basra supports the dominant Hanafi position.

Core Idea
For Abu Yusuf, revived land's tax status depends on vicinity; the Hanafi school holds it is always 'ushr, confirmed by the Companions' consensus on Basra.

In this lesson, we examine an internal Hanafi disagreement over the classification of revived dead land (ihya' al-mawat). While the majority of the school holds that any revived land becomes 'ushr land, Abu Yusuf introduced a location-based criterion. The text uses the consensus of the Companions on Basra to reinforce the school's established position.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the general Hanafi ruling: revived land becomes 'ushr land irrespective of vicinity. This is the view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
This is the mufta bihi position.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Abu Yusuf holds that the classification depends on the vicinity (hayyiz): if adjacent to kharaj land, it becomes kharaj; if adjacent to 'ushr land, it becomes 'ushr.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Abu Yusuf's reasoning is that land takes the ruling of its surroundings, likely based on custom or istihsan. No explicit textual proof is cited here.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The text does not give a direct rebuttal but invokes ijma' al-sahabah that Basra is 'ushr land, implying that vicinity does not override the general rule.
Consensus of the Companions serves as a strong proof.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: under the dominant view, a reviver pays 'ushr (10% or 5%); under Abu Yusuf's view, if near kharaj land, the tax could be higher (kharaj).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ أَحْيَا أَرْضًا مَوَاتًا فَعِنْدَ أَبِي يُوسُفَ هِيَ مُعْتَبَرَةٌ بِحَيْزِهَا فَإِنْ كَانَتْ مِنْ حَيْزِ أَرْضِ الْخَرَاجِ فَهِيَ خَرَاجِيَّةٌ وَإِنْ كَانَتْ مِنْ حَيْزِ أَرْضِ الْعُشْرِ فَهِيَ عُشْرِيَّةٌ وَالْبَصْرَةُ عِنْدَنَا عُشْرِيَّةٌ بِإِجْمَاعِ الصَّحَابَةِ – رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمْ -
And whoever revives a dead land, then according to Abu Yusuf it is considered by its vicinity: if it is within the vicinity of kharaj land, it is kharaji; and if it is within the vicinity of 'ushr land, it is 'ushri. And Basra, according to us, is 'ushri by consensus of the Companions (may Allah be pleased with them).
Source pages p. 389

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the classification of revived dead land (mawat). The default Hanafi rule is that reviving dead land makes it 'ushr land regardless of location. However, Abu Yusuf holds that the classification depends on the vicinity: if the revived land is adjacent to kharaj land, it becomes kharaj land; if adjacent to 'ushr land, it becomes 'ushr. The author then affirms the Hanafi position that Basra is 'ushr land by consensus of the Companions (ijma' al-Sahabah), indicating that Basra was revived from dead land in the 'ushr zone, so all revived land around Basra is 'ushr. The phrase 'indana (according to us) indicates the relied-upon Hanafi position is that Basra is 'ushr, and by extension, Abu Yusuf's rule is not applied to Basra. The authority weight is from the matn, with the consensus of the Companions being a strong proof.

Key Terms
إحياء الموات (ihya' al-mawat): The act of bringing barren or dead land into cultivation, which grants ownership.
حَيْز (hayyiz): Vicinity or adjoining area; used by Abu Yusuf to determine land classification.
إجماع الصحابة (ijma' al-sahabah): Consensus of the Companions of the Prophet, considered a strong proof.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Yusuf, how is revived dead land classified?
A) Always as 'ushr land
B) According to the religion of the reviver
C) Based on the vicinity: if near kharaj land it is kharaj, if near 'ushr land it is 'ushr
D) It remains dead land until the state decides

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, revived dead land is 'ushr tax land according to the dominant view, but Abu Yusuf's vicinity-based rule represents a valid minority position.
