Will of a Mukatab is Invalid
Ruling on the invalidity of a mukatab's will with three proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a mukatab's will and identify the three textual proofs (qawl sahabi, qawl tabi'i, hadith) supporting it.

Core Idea
A mukatab's will is invalid — even with wealth — because he remains a slave with incomplete legal capacity.

In this passage from Al-Quduri, the author lays down a clear ruling: the will of a mukatab is not valid, even if he possesses sufficient wealth to pay off his kitabah. To demonstrate the strength of this position, the commentator provides three proofs from different levels of authority: the saying of a Companion, the saying of a Successor, and a Prophetic hadith. Let us walk through each proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
Recognise that the matn states: 'وَصِيَّةُ الْمُكَاتَبِ لا تَصِحُ' (the will of a mukatab is not valid) and adds the condition 'وَإِنْ تَرَكَ وَفَاءً' (even if he leaves sufficiency). This clarifies that possession of enough wealth does not change the ruling.
2
Locate the first proof (qawl sahabi)
Find the statement attributed to Ibn Abbas (رضي الله عنه) that a slave cannot make a will. This establishes that the mukatab, still a slave, lacks testamentary capacity.
Source: Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, no. 30872
3
Locate the second proof (qawl tabi'i)
Find the statement of Al-Hasan al-Basri that a mukatab cannot free a slave or give a gift without his master's permission. By analogy, making a will (also a gratuitous disposition) is similarly invalid.
Source: Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, no. 30831
4
Locate the third proof (hadith)
Find the Prophetic hadith: 'Any slave who contracts kitabah for one hundred uqiyyah and pays all but ten uqiyyah, he is still a slave.' This directly proves that incomplete payment maintains slave status, thus blocking testamentary capacity.
Source: Ibn Majah, no. 2519; Bukhari, no. 2564
5
Analyse the cumulative evidence
Notice that each proof reinforces the same conclusion: the mukatab remains a slave. The combination of a Companion's verdict, a Successor's ruling, and a Prophetic text gives the Hanafi position strong support.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا تَصِحُ وَصِيَّةُ الْمُكَاتَبِ وَإِنْ تَرَكَ وَفَاءً
وجه (۱) قول الصحابى لثبوت وَلَا تَصِحُ وَصِيَّةُ الْمُكَاتَبِ وَإِنْ تَرَكَ وَفَاءًا عَنْ جُنْدُبٍ قَالَ: سَأَلَ طَهْمَانُ ابْنَ عَبَّاسٍ: أَيُوصِي الْعَبْدُ؟ قَالَ: «لا» (مصنف ابن ابي شيبه، نمبر30872/مصنف عبدالرزاق، الرَّجُل يُوصِي لِأُمِّهِ وَهِيَ أُمُّ وَلَدِ لِأَبِيهِ، وَالَّذِي يُوصِي لِعَبْدِهِ، وَالْوَصِيَّةُ تَهْلَكُ، غبر 16465)
وجه:(۲) قول التابعى لثبوت وَلَا تَصِحُ وَصِيَّةُ الْمُكَاتَبِ وَإِنْ تَرَكَ وَفَاءً عَنِ الْحَسَنِ قَالَ: «الْمُكَاتَبُ لَا يَعْتِقُ وَلَا يَهَبُ إِلَّا بِإِذْنِ مَوْلَاهُ» (مصنف ابن ابي شيبه، الْمُكَاتَبُ يُوصِي أَوْ يَهَبُ أَوْ يَعْتِقُ، أَيَجُوزُ ذَلِكَ، نمبر 30831)
وجه : (۳) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا تَصِحُ وَصِيَّةُ الْمُكَاتَبِ وَإِنْ تَرَكَ وَفَاءً عَنْ عَمْرِو بْنِ شُعَيْبٍ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ، عَنْ جَدِهِ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «أَيُّمَا عَبْدِ كُوتِبَ عَلَى مِائَةِ أُوقِيَّةٍ، فَأَدَّاهَا إِلَّا عَشْرَ أُوقِيَّاتٍ ، فَهُوَ رَقِيقٌ» (سنن ابن ماجه، بَابُ الْمُكَاتَبِ، غمبر 2519/ بخاري شريف ، بَابُ بَيْع الْمُكَاتَبِ إِذَا رَضِيَ، نمبر 2564)
And the will of a mukatab is not valid even if he leaves sufficiency. [Proofs follow]
Source pages p. 426

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling from Al-Quduri that the will of a mukatab (a slave who has contracted with his master to earn his freedom) is invalid, even if he possesses enough wealth to complete his kitabah. The commentator provides three proofs: (1) a saying of the Companion Ibn Abbas that a slave cannot make a will; (2) a saying of the Tabi'i Al-Hasan that a mukatab cannot free or gift without permission; (3) a hadith from the Prophet (saw) that a mukatab who fails to pay all but a small amount remains a slave. These all support the Hanafi position that a mukatab lacks full legal capacity to dispose of property by will.

Key Terms
المكاتب (al-mukatab): A slave who has entered into a contract (kitabah) with his master to pay a sum in exchange for freedom.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on the will of a mukatab who has enough wealth to pay his kitabah?
A) Valid, because he owns the wealth
B) Invalid, even if he has enough wealth
C) Valid only if the master permits
D) Valid only for a third of his wealth

Key Takeaway
The will of a mukatab is invalid because he remains a slave with incomplete legal capacity, even if he has sufficient wealth to complete his kitabah.

Revocation of a Will: Methods and Proofs
Ruling on permissibility and methods of revocation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on revocation of a will and identify the methods of revocation (explicit and implicit).

Core Idea
A testator may revoke his will at any time; revocation can be explicit or implied by actions.

In Hanafi fiqh, a will (wasiyyah) is not binding until death. This lesson examines the permissibility of revocation and the methods by which a testator can effectively cancel his will. The source passage from Al-Quduri presents the ruling with supporting proofs from the Sunnah and the practice of the Companions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
State the legal ruling: it is permissible (mubah) for the testator to revoke his will. Understand that this is because the will is not a binding contract; ownership remains with the testator until death.
Revocation is ja'iz (permissible) in Hanafi school.
2
Recognize the Two Methods
Revocation can be either explicit (saying 'I revoke my will') or implicit (doing an act that clearly indicates revocation, such as selling the bequeathed property). Both are equally effective.
Implicit revocation includes any action inconsistent with the will.
3
Examine the First Proof
The hadith from Aisha (ra) shows that the testator may write in his will that he reserves the right to change it. This indicates that changing or revoking is allowed.
Hadith source: Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab al-Ruju' fi al-Wasiyyah.
4
Examine the Second Proof
Umar's statement 'a man may change his will as he wishes' is a direct proof of permissibility. Another report from Umar specifically mentions revoking a bequest made during illness.
These are qawl al-sahabi, which is a valid proof in Hanafi usul.
5
Understand the Usul Principle
The Urdu note states that whether explicitly or by implication, the will is ended. This aligns with the Hanafi principle that intent can be expressed through actions (dalalah).
Both forms of ruju' nullify the will.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيَجُوزُ لِلْمُوصِي الرُّجُوعُ عَنْ الْوَصِيَّةِ . فَإِذَا صَرَّحَ بِالرُّجُوعِ أَوْ فَعَلَ مَا يَدُلُّ عَلَى الرُّجُوعِ كَانَ رُجُوعًا
وجه (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَيَجُوزُ لِلْمُوصِي الرُّجُوعُ عَنْ الْوَصِيَّةِ عَنْ عَائِشَةَ قَالَتْ: لِيَكْتُبِ الرَّجُلُ فِي وَصِيَّتِهِ: إِنْ حَدَثَ بِي حَدَثُ مَوْتِي قَبْلَ أَنْ أُغَيِّرَ وَصِيَّتِي هَذِهِ. وَرُوِيَ عَنْ عُمَرَ بنِ الْخَطَّابِ أَنَّهُ قَالَ: يُغَيِّرُ الرَّجُلُ مَا شَاءَ مِنَ الْوَصِيَّةِ (السنن الكبري للبيهقي، بَابُ الرُّجُوعِ فِي الْوَصِيَّةِ وَتَغْيِيرِهَا ، نمبر 12654)
وجه (۲) قول الصحابى لثبوت وَيَجُوزُ لِلْمُوصِي الرُّجُوعُ عَنْ الْوَصِيَّةِ قَالَ عُمَرُ: «مَا أَعْتَقَ الرَّجُلُ فِي مَرَضِهِ مِنْ رَقِيقِهِ فَهِيَ وَصِيَّةٌ إِنْ شَاءَ رَجَعَ فِيهَا» (مصنف ابن ابي شيبه، الرَّجُلُ يُوصِي بالْوَصِيَّةِ ثُمَّ يُريدُ أَنْ يُغَيْرَهَا ، نمبر 30805)
اصول : دمیت ختم کرنے کے لئے صراحتا رجوع کرے یا دلالۃ، بہر صورت وصیت ختم ہو جائے گی۔
And it is permissible for the testator to revoke the will. So if he explicitly revokes or does something that indicates revocation, it is a revocation. [Proofs follow] Usul: For ending the will, whether explicitly or by implication, in any case the will ends.
Source pages p. 426

Commentary
This passage states the ruling that a testator may revoke his will at any time during his life. The revocation can be explicit (saying 'I revoke my will') or implicit (doing an act that clearly shows revocation, e.g., selling the bequeathed property). Two proofs are provided: a report from Aisha about writing in the will that one may change it, and a saying of Umar that a man may revoke a bequest made during illness. The usul note in Urdu emphasizes that both explicit and implicit revocation end the will.

Key Terms
الرجوع (al-ruju'): Revocation of a will by the testator during his lifetime.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following would NOT constitute a valid revocation of a will according to this passage?
A) The testator says 'I revoke my will'
B) The testator sells the property he bequeathed
C) The testator destroys the written will document
D) The testator denies having made a will

Key Takeaway
The testator can revoke his will at any time by explicit statement or any action that clearly indicates his intent to cancel the will.

Denying a Will is Not Revocation; Bequest to Neighbors
Ruling that denial of a will is not revocation, and definition of neighbors for bequest.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that denial of a will does not revoke it, and define 'neighbors' (jiiran) according to Abu Hanifa's position, supported by the cited dalil.

Core Idea
Denying a will does not cancel it; only explicit revocation, not mere denial, affects the bequest.

This passage from Al-Quduri presents two clear legal rulings: first, a testator's mere denial of having made a will does not count as a valid revocation in Hanafi law; second, if a testator bequeaths to 'his neighbors', Abu Hanifa restricts this to those whose houses are physically adjacent. While the first ruling is supported by hadith and athar, the second is stated as a positional definition. Understanding these rulings helps distinguish between actions that invalidate a will and those that do not, and clarifies who qualifies as a beneficiary under a general bequest.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
Read the Arabic text and locate the two separate hukm statements: (1) 'وَمَنْ جَحَدَ الْوَصِيَّةَ لَمْ يَكُنْ رُجُوعًا' (denial is not revocation) and (2) 'وَمَنْ أَوْصَى لِجِيرَانِهِ فَهُمُ الْمُلَاصِقُونَ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ' (bequest to neighbors means adjacent ones per Abu Hanifa). Note that the first ruling is followed by proofs, the second is stated without dalil in this passage.
The proofs that follow are only for the first ruling, though they discuss neighbors; this can be confusing if not parsed carefully.
2
Parse the first ruling and key term
The key term is 'الجحود' (juhud) meaning denial. In Hanafi law, denial of a will does not constitute a valid form of revocation (ruju'). Only explicit words or clear acts of revocation nullify a will. Understand that a testator may deny due to forgetfulness or strategy, but the will remains enforceable.
Contrast with Shafi'i view where denial is considered implied revocation.
3
Examine the proofs for the first ruling
The passage provides three proofs: (1) Hadith from Aisha about giving gifts to the nearest neighbor (showing priority of proximity), (2) Hadith about the duty of the neighbor of the mosque to pray in the mosque, (3) Statement of Ali emphasizing the same duty. Although these focus on neighborly rights, the commentator uses them to support the first ruling by analogy: if denying a will revoked it, the neighbor would lose the bequest, but the hadith underscores the neighbor's persisting right. This is a weak connection but present in the text.
The proofs are zanni in thubut and dalala; they are not the strongest dalil, but suffice for the ruling.
4
Parse the second ruling and intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
For a bequest to 'neighbors', Abu Hanifa restricts it to 'الملاصقون' (those whose houses physically touch). The two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that it includes all residents of the same lane or alley. The passage only states Abu Hanifa's view without further reasoning.
The mufta bihi on this issue may vary; later Hanafi texts often adopt the wider definition.
5
Contrast with cross-madhhab difference
On the first ruling, Imam al-Shafi'i considers denial as an implicit revocation (ruju'), based on the principle that actions speak louder than words. The Hanafi response is that revocation is a legal act requiring explicit expression; mere denial does not meet the threshold. This difference has practical consequences in estate distribution.
The thamarah al-khilaf is whether the will is executed or not after such denial.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ جَحَدَ الْوَصِيَّةَ لَمْ يَكُنْ رُجُوعًا
وَمَنْ أَوْصَى لِجِيرَانِهِ فَهُمُ الْمُلَاصِقُونَ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ
وجه : (ا) الحديث لثبوت وَمَنْ جَحَدَ الْوَصِيَّةَ لَمْ يَكُنْ رُجُوعًا سَمِعْتُ طَلْحَةَ بْنَ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ، عَنْ عَائِشَةَ قَالَتْ: قُلْتُ: يَا رَسُولَ اللهِ، إِنَّ لِي جَارَيْنِ، فَإِلَى أَيْهِمَا أُهْدِي؟ قَالَ: إِلَى أَقْرَهِمَا مِنْكِ بَابًا (بخاري شريف ، بَابٌ : أَيُّ الْجِوَارِ أَقْرَبُ، غمبر 2259)
وجه :(ا) دليل الصاحبين الحديث لثبوت وَمَنْ جَحَدَ الْوَصِيَّةَ لَمْ يَكُنْ رُجُوعًا عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ ، قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم : « لَا صَلَاةَ لِجَارِ الْمَسْجِدِ إِلَّا فِي الْمَسْجِدِ» (سنن دارقطني، بَابُ الْحَةِ لِجَارِ الْمَسْجِدِ عَلَى الصَّلَاةِ فِيهِ إِلَّا مِنْ عُذْرٍ ، نمبر 1553)
وجه :(۲) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَمَنْ جَحَدَ الْوَصِيَّةَ لَمْ يَكُنْ رُجُوعًا عَنْ عَلِيٍّ ، قَالَ: «مَنْ كَانَ جَارَ الْمَسْجِدِ فَسَمِعَ الْمُنَادِيَ يُنَادِي فَلَمْ يُجِبْهُ مِنْ غَيْرِ عُذْرٍ فَلَا صَلَاةَ لَهُ» (سنن دارقطني، بَابُ الْحَةِ لِجَارِ الْمَسْجِدِ عَلَى الصَّلَاةِ فِيهِ إِلَّا مِنْ عُذْرٍ غمبر 1554)
وجه : (۱) دليل الشافعى الحديث لثبوت وَمَنْ جَحَدَ الْوَصِيَّةَ لَمْ يَكُنْ رُجُوعًا عَنْ عَائِشَةَ ، أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ : «أَوْصَانِي جِبْرِيلُ بِالْجَارِ إِلَى أَرْبَعِينَ دَارًا، عَشَرَةً مِنْ هَا هُنَا، وَعَشَرَةً مِنْ هَا هُنَا، وَعَشَرَةً مِنْ هَا هُنَا، وَعَشَرَةً مِنْ هَا هُنَا» (بخاري شريف ، بَابُ الرَّجُلِ يَقُولُ: ثُلُثُ مَالِي إِلَى فَلَانٍ يَضَعُهُ حَيْثُ أَرَاهُ اللَّهُ، وَمَا يَخْتَارُ لِلْمُوصَى إِلَيْهِ أَنْ يُعْطِيَهُ أَهْلَ الْحَاجَةِ مِنْ قَرَابَةِ الْمَيِّتِ حَتَّى يُغْنِيَهُمْ ثُمَّ رُضَعَاءَهُ ثُمَّ جِيرَانَهُ، نمبر 12612)
And whoever denies the will, it is not a revocation. And whoever bequeaths to his neighbors, they are the adjacent ones according to Abu Hanifa. [Proofs follow]
Source pages p. 427

Commentary
This passage contains two rulings. First, if a testator denies having made a will (juhud), this denial does not count as revocation; the will remains valid unless he explicitly revokes. Second, if a testator bequeaths to 'his neighbors', according to Abu Hanifa the neighbors are those whose houses are adjacent (mulasiqun), not the wider neighborhood. The proofs provided are for the first ruling: hadiths about the rights of neighbors, showing that neighborly rights are strong but do not affect revocation. The mention of neighbors in the proofs supports the definition of neighbor as one whose house is next door.

Key Terms
الجحود (al-juhud): Denial by the testator that he made a will, which does not revoke it.
الملاصقون (al-mulasiqun): Neighbors whose houses physically adjoin the testator's house.
الرجوع (al-ruju'): Revocation of a will by explicit statement or action.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if a person bequeaths to 'his neighbors', who are included?
A) All residents of the same street
B) Only those whose houses are adjacent to his
C) All Muslims in the locality
D) Only relatives who live nearby

Key Takeaway
Denial of a will is not a valid revocation; the will stands until explicitly revoked, and a bequest to 'neighbors' means only adjacent houses per Abu Hanifa.

Bequest to In-laws (As-har) and Sons-in-law (Akhtan): Hanafi Definitions
Ruling on bequest to in-laws: meaning of 'as-har' and 'akhtan'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definitions of 'as-har' and 'akhtan' in a bequest, apply them to identify recipients, and explain the proof from the hadith of Juwayriyah.

Core Idea
A bequest to in-laws (as-har) goes to the wife's mahram relatives; a bequest to sons-in-law (akhtan) goes to the husbands of one's own mahram female relatives.

This lesson clarifies how the Hanafi school interprets the terms 'as-har' and 'akhtan' when they appear in a will. The distinction is crucial: one refers to the testator's wife's family, the other to the husbands of his own female relatives. The ruling is supported by the practice of the Companions regarding the Prophet's marriage to Juwayriyah bint al-Harith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two terms
Recognize that the passage defines two distinct categories: as-har (الأصهار) and akhtan (الأختان). As-har refers to the wife's mahram relatives; akhtan refers to husbands of one's own mahram female relatives.
The English terms 'in-laws' and 'sons-in-law' are approximate; the Arabic terms are precise.
2
State the Hanafi definitions
Based on the text: as-har = every mahram relative of the testator's wife. akhtan = each husband of a mahram female relative of the testator (e.g., daughter, sister).
Mahram means a relative whom one cannot marry due to blood or marriage proximity.
3
Connect definitions to mahram
Note that the definitions are built on the concept of mahram. As-har are mahram to the wife; akhtan are husbands of women who are mahram to the testator.
This ensures the relationship is close enough to be recognized in Islamic inheritance and family law.
4
Analyze the hadith proof
The hadith describes that when the Prophet married Juwayriyah, her tribe (Banu al-Mustaliq) were freed because they became 'as-har' of the Prophet. This shows that as-har means the wife's relatives.
The Companions explicitly used the term 'as-har' for the wife's tribe, confirming the Hanafi definition.
5
Consider the condition (usul note)
The Urdu note states that the in-law relationship is valid only if the marriage exists at the time of the testator's death. If the wife is divorced or deceased, her relatives are no longer as-har.
This condition affects the execution of the bequest.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ أَوْصَى لِأَصْهَارِهِ فَالْوَصِيَّةُ لِكُلِّ ذِي رَحِمٍ مَحْرَمٍ مِنْ امْرَأَتِهِ وَإِنْ أَوْصَى لِأَخْتَانِهِ فَالْخَتَنُ زَوْجُ كُلِّ ذَاتِ رَحِمٍ مَحْرَمٍ مِنْهُ
٢٩ وجه : (۱) الْحَدِيث لثبوت وَمَنْ أَوْصَى لِأَصْهَارِهِ فَالْوَصِيَّةُ لِكُلِّ ذِي رَحِمٍ مَحْرَمٍ عَنْ عَائِشَةَ قَالَتْ: وَقَعَتْ جُوَيْرِيَةُ بِنْتُ الْحَارِثِ بْنِ الْمُصْطَلِقِ فِي سَهُم ثَابِتِ بْنِ قَيْسِ بْنِ شَمَّاسِ، أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَدْ تَزَوَّجَ جُوَيْرِيَةَ، فَأَرْسَلُوا مَا فِي أَيْدِيهِمْ مِنَ السَّبْيِ، فَأَعْتَقُوهُمْ، وَقَالُوا: أَصْهَارُ رَسُولِ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم . فَمَا رَأَيْنَا امْرَأَةً كَانَتْ أَعْظَمَ بَرَكَةً عَلَى قَوْمِهَا مِنْهَا، أُعْتِقَ فِي سَبَبِهَا مِائَةُ أَهْلِ بَيْتٍ مِنْ بَنِي الْمُصْطَلِقِ (سنن ابوداود، بَابٌ فِي بَيْعِ الْمُكَاتَبِ إِذَا فُسِخَتِ الْكِتَابَةُ، نمبر 3931)
اصول: موصی کے موت کے وقت بیوی سے نکاح باقی ہو تب ہی مہر کی رشتہ داری رہے گی۔
And whoever bequeaths to his in-laws (as-har), the bequest is for every mahram relative of his wife. And if he bequeaths to his sons-in-law (akhtan), then the khatan is the husband of every mahram relative of his. [Proof follows] Usul: At the time of the testator's death, only if the marriage with his wife remains intact does the in-law relationship persist.
Source pages p. 427

Commentary
This passage clarifies the interpretation of 'as-har' (in-laws) and 'akhtan' (sons-in-law / brothers-in-law) in a will. According to the Hanafi school, if a testator bequeaths to his as-har, it includes all mahram relatives of his wife (e.g., her father, brother, uncle). If he bequeaths to his akhtan, that refers to the husbands of his own mahram female relatives (e.g., his daughter's husband, his sister's husband). The proof is the story of Juwayriyah bint al-Harith, whose marriage to the Prophet (saw) caused her tribe to be freed because they became in-laws of the Prophet. The usul note in Urdu states that the in-law relationship is only relevant if the marriage is still valid at the time of the testator's death; if divorce or death has occurred, the in-law relationship is severed.

Key Terms
الأصهار (al-as-har): The mahram relatives of the testator's wife (e.g., her father, brother, maternal uncle).
الأختان (al-akhtan): The husbands of the testator's mahram female relatives (e.g., daughter's husband, sister's husband).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a man bequeaths to his 'as-har', who receives the bequest?
A) His wife's mahram relatives
B) His own mahram female relatives
C) The husbands of his daughters
D) All his relatives by marriage

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, 'as-har' and 'akhtan' in a will refer to specific categories of in-laws: wife's mahram relatives (as-har) and husbands of one's own mahram female relatives (akhtan), as derived from the practice of the Companions.

Bequest to Relatives: Determining the Closest Kin
Ruling on bequest to relatives with intra-Hanafi dispute over paternal vs maternal uncle priority

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on bequest to relatives and apply the rule of closeness to determine distribution in the case of paternal and maternal uncles.

Core Idea
When a bequest is made to relatives, the closest mahram relatives take priority, with paternal uncles favored over maternal uncles per Abu Hanifa.

In this lesson, we examine a key ruling from Kitab al-Wasaya on bequests to relatives. The passage establishes the principle of giving to the nearest mahram relative, then the next nearest, and addresses a specific dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, regarding the distribution when both paternal and maternal uncles exist.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled? A bequest made to 'aqarib' (relatives). The ruling: the bequest must be given to the nearest mahram relative, then the next nearest, excluding parents and children.
The bequest must be to at least two persons (plural indicated).
2
Locate the dalil
What proofs does the author cite? Quranic verses (Baqarah 2:180, 2:215), a statement of the Tabi'i Tawus, and two hadith: 'Give shares to the nearest male relative' (Bukhari) and 'The maternal uncle inherits for one who has no heir' (Tirmidhi).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How do the proofs support the ruling? The Quran commands bequest to relatives ('aqriba'), and the hadith establish priority for the nearest male agnate, applied analogically to bequests.
The phrase 'bil-ma'ruf' in the verse leaves distribution details to ijtihad.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
What is the intra-Hanafi dispute? Abu Hanifa: paternal uncles take all (or half if one paternal uncle is present). Sahibayn: all relatives share proportionally based on farthest common ancestor in Islam.
This is an ikhtilaf within the school, not between madhhabs.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Which position is mufta bihi? Abu Hanifa's view is the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school, as presented in al-Quduri and confirmed in later texts like al-Hidayah.
The Sahibayn's view is respected but not the operative fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الوصايا
٣٠ وَمَنْ أَوْصَى لِأَقَارِبِهِ فَالْوَصِيَّةُ لِلْأَقْرَبِ فَالْأَقْرَبِ مِنْ كُلِّ ذِي رَحِمٍ تَحْرَمٍ مِنْهُ وَلَا يَدْخُلُ فِيهِمْ الْوَالِدَانِ وَالْوَلَدُ وَتَكُونُ لِلاثْنَيْنِ فَصَاعِدًا فَإِذَا أَوْصَى بِذَلِكَ وَلَهُ عَمَّانٍ وَخَالَانِ فَالْوَصِيَّةُ لِعَمَّيْهِ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَإِنْ كَانَ لَهُ عَمَّ وَخَالَانِ فَلِلْعَمَ النِّصْفُ وَلِلْخَالَيْنِ النِّصْفُ وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ الْوَصِيَّةُ لِكُلِّ مَنْ يُنْسَبُ إِلَى أَقْصَى أَبٍ لَهُ فِي الْإِسْلَامِ
وجه: (1) الآية لثبوت وَمَنْ أَوْصَى لِأَقَارِبِهِ فَالْوَصِيَّةُ لِلْأَقْرَبِ: ﴿كُتِبَ عَلَيْكُمْ إِذَا حَضَرَ أَحَدَكُمُ الْمَوْتُ إِن تَرَكَ خَيْرًا الْوَصِيَّةُ لِلْوَالِدَيْنِ وَالْأَقْرَبِينَ بِالْمَعْرُوفِ حَقًّا عَلَى الْمُتَّقِينَ﴾ (سورة البقرة، 180)
وجه: (٢) الآية لثبوت وَمَنْ أَوْصَى لِأَقَارِبِهِ فَالْوَصِيَّةُ لِلْأَقْرَبِ: ﴿يَسْأَلُونَكَ مَاذَا يُنفِقُونَ قُلْ مَا أَنفَقْتُم مِّنْ خَيْرٍ فَلِلْوَالِدَيْنِ وَالْأَقْرَبِينَ وَالْيَتَامَى وَالْمَسَاكِينِ وَابْنِ السَّبِيلِ﴾ (سورة البقرة، 215)
وجه: (۳) قول التابعى لثبوت وَمَنْ أَوْصَى لِأَقَارِبِهِ فَالْوَصِيَّةُ لِلْأَقْرَبِ: عَنِ ابْنِ طَاوُسٍ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ، قَالَ: «كَانَ لَا يَرَى الْوَصِيَّةَ إِلَّا لِذَوِي الْأَرْحَامِ أَهْلِ الْفَقْرِ، فَإِنْ أَوْصَى بِمَا لِغَيْرِهِمْ نُزِعَتْ مِنْهُمْ فَرُدَّتْ إِلَيْهِمْ، فَإِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ فِيهِمْ فُقَرَاءُ فَلِأَهْلِ الْفَقْرِ مَنْ كَانُوا، وَإِنْ بَقِيَ أَهْلُهَا إِلَّا مَنْ يُوصِي لَهُمْ» (مصنف ابن أبي شيبة، رقم 30783)
وجه: (۱) الحديث لثبوت فَإِذَا أَوْصَى بِذَلِكَ وَلَهُ عَمَّانِ: عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ : «أَلْحِقُوا الْفَرَائِضَ بِأَهْلِهَا، فَمَا بَقِيَ فَهُوَ لِأَوْلَى رَجُلٍ ذَكَرٍ» (صحيح البخاري، باب ميراث ابن الابن، رقم 6735)
وجه: (٢) الحديث لثبوت فَإِذَا أَوْصَى بِذَلِكَ وَلَهُ عَمَّانِ: عَنْ عَائِشَةَ قَالَتْ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم : «الْخَالُ وَارِثُ مَنْ لَا وَارِثَ لَهُ» (سنن الترمذي، باب ميراث الخال، رقم 2104)
Book of Bequests
30. Whoever makes a bequest to his relatives, the bequest is for the nearest then the nearest of every mahram relative, and parents and children are not included among them, and it is for two or more. So if he makes a bequest to that effect and he has two paternal uncles and two maternal uncles, then the bequest is for his two paternal uncles according to Abu Hanifa. And if he has one paternal uncle and two maternal uncles, then for the paternal uncle is half and for the two maternal uncles is half. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: The bequest is for everyone who is traced back to the farthest ancestor in Islam.
Proof (1) of the verse for establishing that whoever makes a bequest to his relatives the bequest is for the nearest: {Prescribed for you when death approaches any of you, if he leaves good, to make a bequest for parents and relatives with what is recognized as proper, an obligation upon the righteous.} (Baqarah 180)
Proof (2) of the verse: {They ask you what they should spend. Say: Whatever good you spend is for parents, relatives, orphans, the needy, and the wayfarer.} (Baqarah 215)
Proof (3) of the statement of the Tabi'i: Ibn Tawus from his father: He did not consider a bequest except for poor relatives, so if he made a bequest for other than them, it is taken from them and returned to them. If among them there are no poor, then for the poor wherever they are, even if they are relatives except those to whom he makes a bequest. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, no. 30783)
Proof (1) of the hadith for establishing that when he makes a bequest and he has two paternal uncles: Ibn Abbas: The Messenger of Allah said: Give the obligatory shares to their recipients, and what remains is for the nearest male relative. (Bukhari, no. 6735)
Proof (2) of the hadith: Aisha: The Messenger of Allah said: The maternal uncle inherits for one who has no heir. (Tirmidhi, no. 2104)
Source pages p. 428

Commentary
This is a ruling from Kitab al-Wasaya on bequests to relatives. The passage first states the general rule: when someone makes a bequest to 'aqarib' (relatives), the distribution is given to the nearest mahram relative, then the next nearest, and so on. Parents and children are excluded because they already have fixed shares in inheritance. The bequest must be to at least two persons, as a plural. Then a specific case is given: if the testator has two paternal uncles (from father's side) and two maternal uncles (from mother's side), according to Imam Abu Hanifa the bequest goes entirely to the paternal uncles because they are closer in legal relationship (asabah). If there is one paternal uncle and two maternal uncles, Abu Hanifa says the paternal uncle gets half and the two maternal uncles share the other half, because the paternal uncle is closer than each maternal uncle individually, but the maternal uncles collectively outnumber. Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad differ: they say the bequest is distributed according to lineage, tracing each relative back to the farthest ancestor in Islam, so that all relatives share proportionally. The proofs provided include Quranic verses emphasizing bequest to relatives, a statement of the tabi'i Tawus (father of Ibn Tawus) showing the early practice of restricting bequests to poor relatives, and hadiths on inheritance rules being applied to bequests by analogy.

Key Terms
أقارب (aqārib): Relatives; in this context, those who are mahram (forbidden in marriage) by blood, excluding parents and children.
ذو رحم محرم (dhū raḥim muḥarram): A relative through blood who is permanently forbidden in marriage (mahram), such as uncles, aunts, siblings, etc.
الأقرب فالأقرب (al-aqrab fa al-aqrab): The nearest then the nearest; the principle of prioritizing the closest mahram relative in distribution.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if a testator makes a bequest to his 'aqarib' and has two paternal uncles and two maternal uncles, who receives the bequest?
A) All four uncles share equally.
B) The two paternal uncles receive the entire bequest.
C) The maternal uncles receive half and paternal half.
D) Only the maternal uncles receive the bequest.

Key Takeaway
When making a bequest to relatives, the Hanafi school requires distribution to the nearest mahram relatives, prioritizing paternal agnates over maternal ones, as established by Imam Abu Hanifa.

Bequest of a Third When Part of Property Is Destroyed
Ruling on bequest of a fraction when the property is partially destroyed

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on bequests when a portion of the bequeathed property is destroyed before execution.

Core Idea
When two-thirds of bequeathed property is destroyed, the legatee receives the entire remaining portion within the estate's one-third limit.

A common question in bequests involves partial destruction of the specified property. How should the legacy be calculated? This lesson unpacks a clear ruling from Al-Quduri: if a testator bequeaths one-third of a specific asset and two-thirds of that asset are destroyed before death, the legatee takes all that remains, provided it does not exceed the estate's one-third limit. We will examine the reasoning and the Quranic proof behind this rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the bequest and its limit
Note that the bequest is of a fraction (one-third) of a specific type of property (dirhams or sheep). Under Hanafi law, a bequest to a non-heir cannot exceed one-third of the total estate.
If the bequest were of a specific item rather than a fraction, the rule might differ.
2
Determine the effect of partial destruction
The passage assumes two-thirds of the specified property are destroyed before the testator's death. Only one-third of the original amount remains.
Destruction means the property no longer exists at death.
3
Apply the one-third rule to the remaining property
The testator bequeathed one-third of the original. After destruction, the remaining one-third is exactly what was bequeathed. The ruling states this remaining portion is taken from the estate's one-third allowed for bequests, and the legatee receives all of it.
If the remaining portion were larger than one-third of the total estate, the heirs' consent would be needed.
4
Consider the proof and principle
The Quranic verse (4:12) speaks of partners in the third. The principle derived is that plural in inheritance indicates at least two, and by analogy, a bequest to multiple recipients requires at least two recipients. Here, the proof supports the validity of fractional bequests.
The dalala of the verse is zanni (conjectural) because the application to this scenario is via analogy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٣٢ وَمَنْ أَوْصَى لِرَجُلٍ بِثُلُثِ دَرَاهِمِهِ أَوْ بِثُلُثِ غَنَمِهِ فَهَلَكَ ثُلُثَا ذَلِكَ وَبَقِيَ ثُلُثُهُ وَهُوَ يَخْرُجُ مِنْ ثُلُثِ مَا بَقِيَ مِنْ مَالِهِ فَلَهُ جَمِيعُ مَا بَقِيَ
وجه: (1) الآية لثبوت وَمَنْ أَوْصَى لِرَجُلٍ بِثُلُثِ دَرَاهِمِهِ: فَإِن كَانُواْ أَكْثَرَ مِن ذَلِكَ فَهُمْ شُرَكَاءُ فِي الثُّلُثِ (سورة النساء، 4:12) اصول: جمع کا صیغہ تین کے لئے آتا ہے، لیکن میراث میں دو کے لئے آتا ہے، وصیت میراث کی بہن ہے، اسلئے کم از کم دو کو شامل ہو گی۔
32. Whoever makes a bequest to a man of one-third of his dirhams or one-third of his sheep, then two-thirds of that are destroyed and one-third remains, and it comes out of one-third of what remains from his property, so he gets all that remains.
Proof (1) of the verse for establishing: 'If they are more than that, then they are partners in the third.' (Nisa 4:12) Principle: The plural form is used for three, but in inheritance it is used for two, and bequest is the sister of inheritance, so it includes at least two.
Source pages p. 428

Commentary
This passage explains a scenario in bequests where the bequeathed item is partially destroyed. If a person bequeaths one-third of his dirhams (money) or one-third of his sheep, and before the bequest is executed, two-thirds of that specific property are destroyed, the legatee receives one-third of what remains of the property, but that comes from the one-third of the total estate that is allowed for bequests. The result is that the legatee gets all the remaining portion of the specified property (the one-third that survived) because it fits within the one-third limit. The proof cited is from Quran 4:12 about sharing in the third, with the principle that plural in Arabic usually indicates three or more, but in inheritance it can indicate two, and since bequest is similar to inheritance (both involve transfer of property after death), the same principle applies: the bequest to multiple individuals requires at least two recipients.

Key Terms
ثلث (thuluth): One-third; the maximum portion of the estate that can be bequeathed to non-heirs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a testator bequeaths one-third of his sheep, and two-thirds of those sheep die before his death, what does the legatee receive?
A) One-third of the original number of sheep.
B) All of the remaining sheep.
C) One-third of the remaining sheep.
D) Nothing, because the bequest is void.

Key Takeaway
When a bequest of a fraction of a specific property is partially destroyed, the legatee takes all that remains provided it is within the estate's one-third limit.
